Local Correspondence

Songjiang 67

Bandits Returned to Court for Trial Near Yexie Town's Maojing Beach, a Chen family was suddenly attacked one evening by over twenty bandits who kidnapped five members of Chen Xingsheng's family, along with Wang Xiaodi and Yao Chengyi, totaling seven people. They also stole a fast-firing rifle with the county seal, heading west. The next day, Chen Shenshi and two others were released in Fengjing, while Chen Gushi and others were taken to the Shanghai Bund. As they were disembarking and about to board a vehicle, intending to hide them in a facility, Chen Gushi encountered a police officer and called for help. The police arrested the female bandit Yang Yinshi, also known as Wu Chenshi, and rescued Wang Xiaodi and two others from a brick and tile boat in Rihui Port. The captured bandits Cao Jiafa and Ye Chishan, along with the boatman Meng Huatang Zhuang Wansheng, were taken back to the district office. After a preliminary interrogation, they were ordered to be handed over to the Songjiang County Government for trial. Upon receiving the report, County Magistrate Jin immediately dispatched Police Chief Dong Futang and bailiffs Wang Fujin and Xu Sheng to Shanghai to escort the bandits Cao Jiafa and others back on the afternoon of the 16th, for questioning and trial.

County Government Burns Opium The County Government of this county had previously accumulated a large amount of confiscated opium paraphernalia and opium, as well as contraband, from seized opium cases. With the approval of the High Court, they were publicly burned yesterday (the 16th) at 2:00 PM.

Fengjing Joint Defense Captures Important Bandits In the villages near Fengjing Town in this county, bandits were rampant. Since the organization of the Joint Defense Office, coordinating the search and arrest of bandits, followed by public execution, the local area has seen some stability. However, many major criminals who escaped are still at large. It has been learned that the Joint Defense Office captured five important bandits the night before last, and they are currently being interrogated.

Wujiang 68

Opium Trafficker Sentenced in Court The day before yesterday, the County Government, acting on a secret order from the Jiangsu High Court, inspected opium trafficking facilities in Tongli. The County Government, upon receiving the order, secretly investigated, led by Secretary Sheng, and discovered over ten catties of opium and two hundred and eighty yuan in banknotes at the Tongxin Inn in Tongli Town. They were escorted to the County Government, and a report was submitted to the court for investigation and handling. By order, the county sentenced the offender. Yesterday (the 14th), Judge Yang conducted a court hearing and sentenced the suspect to one year and ten months of penal servitude, fined one thousand five hundred yuan, and confiscated the opium and banknotes.

Rumors of Child Abduction Cause False Alarm On the afternoon of the 14th, several large boats arrived at the villages of Shilipu in the west gate and Wubuli in the north gate of this city. Six people disembarked with suspicious behavior, and the villagers suspected them of abducting children. For a time, people were fearful and brought their children into the city.

Suzhou 69

County-City Merger Situation The County Government took over the Municipal Government at 9:00 AM yesterday morning (the 16th). County Magistrate Huang, accompanied by commissioners from the provincial departments, went to the Municipal Government to meet with Mayor Lu and the heads of various bureaus and sections. They first held a discussion meeting, and then the commissioners from the provincial departments, together with the heads of various bureaus and sections of the County, separately took over the municipal bureaus and sections. However, the Municipal Government's Secretariat had not yet completed the transfer procedures and will be taken over today (the 17th). Also, the Municipal Public Security Bureau originally had five districts and five teams. The plan to reduce two districts and five branch bureaus in the urban and rural areas is awaiting provincial approval. For now, it has been decided to temporarily maintain the status quo. The security, mounted patrol, and water patrol teams have been taken over by Cao Xiaoping, the captain of the County Police Brigade, who is proceeding to reorganize them into Class A police teams, with two-thirds stationed in various rural areas and one-third remaining in the city for deployment. The detective and fire brigades will be taken over by County Magistrate Huang in consultation with Captain Cao before further review.

Strict Arrest of Major Bandit Leaders Diao Shiqin, the escaped bandit leader from Baoying County, is hiding in Shanghai and is planning to return to Jiangbei to gather desperate individuals in an attempt to cause disturbances. After learning of this through reconnaissance by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, an order was issued yesterday to the troops stationed along the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway to strictly defend and suppress them.

Wuxi 70

Citywide Rumors of Child Abduction Recently, a rumor has suddenly spread in the community of our county, stating that a certain place is building a large bridge and needs a certain number of boys and girls, and that people have been sent out to capture them. It was also said that Cai's Elementary School had lost fourteen students. The rumor spread throughout the city, causing widespread panic. However, after investigation, there was absolutely no such thing. It is clear that malicious individuals were creating rumors and causing trouble. In order to stabilize public sentiment and strictly prohibit the spread of rumors, the County Government and the Public Security Bureau separately issued public notices yesterday to dispel the rumors. At the same time, the Education Bureau also instructed the principals of public and private schools to inform students not to lightly believe rumors and to focus on their studies.

Management Issues of Municipal Funds and Property The Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office was ordered to close down, and the office's various undertakings were handed over to the County Government's various bureaus. The County Government will also form a Municipal Funds and Property Management Committee in conjunction with local figures to manage municipal funds and property. It is learned that the Municipal Preparatory Office was originally scheduled to hand over on the 15th, but due to County Magistrate Sun going to Shanghai for medical treatment, it was decided to postpone the handover by five days. The Reorganization Committee of the County Party Headquarters believes that the Municipal Funds and Property Management Committee after the closure of the Municipal Preparatory Office should be composed of representatives from the Party Headquarters and people's organizations, and should not be controlled by a few special classes. Yesterday, Zhou Fengjing, a member of the Standing Committee of the Party Reorganization Committee, issued an official letter to the County Government stating his views and requesting that they be considered. At the same time, Zhao Zixin, Cai Jihui, Miao Erheng, and others from the First District also believe that the Municipal Funds and Property Committee should be organized by the First District Office in conjunction with impartial local figures, and that the word "District" should be added to the name of the Property Committee to indicate distinction. Therefore, they submitted the above proposal to the Sixth District Affairs Meeting for resolution, and immediately submitted the original proposal to the County Government for adoption and implementation. It is said that the County Government plans to study the various proposals for the Municipal Funds and Property Committee before considering and requesting instructions for handling. Also, Yang Hanxi and Zhou Jimei, residents of the First District, went to Zhenjiang yesterday (the 16th) morning to petition the Provincial Government and the Department of Civil Affairs and Construction for the second time, requesting that the various affairs of the Preparatory Office be handed over to the First District Office for management.

Gloomy Cocoon Market The silkworm market in Wuxi has reached the stage of major sleep and leaf opening, but due to the unfavorable weather and the impact of privately made inferior seeds, the official authorities have not added inspections. As a result, the results in the surrounding villages are extremely poor, with statistics showing only about 30%. Due to the sluggish silk sales and the sharp drop in market prices, cocoon merchants are becoming more pessimistic and are taking a wait-and-see attitude. Those who are preparing to collect cocoons, given the unrest caused by bandits, are sending telegrams to the County Government and the Water Police District for protection.

Changzhou 71

Sudden Change of Public Security Bureau Chief Again Liu Lei, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau of Wuyi, had only been in office for half a month when the Department of Civil Affairs suddenly announced yesterday (the 15th) that Yin Penglai would be appointed to take over, while Liu Lei would be appointed elsewhere.

Police Team Captures a Notorious Bandit The First Squad of the First Company of the police team stationed in Xixiashu, Wuyi, captured a notorious bandit named Qin Rugeng in Wenxiangli the night before last. The squad leader, Liu Yuanshan, escorted him to the brigade headquarters on the 15th and then to the county government that night for interrogation. It is said that the bandit has committed numerous crimes, and threatening letters were also found. He has many accomplices and followers.

Kidnapping Case in Sanshan Township The home of Jiang Canjin, the head of the 13th neighborhood of Tang Village in Sanshan Township, Wuyi, was robbed the night before last, suffering significant losses. Before leaving, the bandits kidnapped his 14-year-old child. The police district in charge sent police to pursue the bandits, who then abandoned the child. The police team bravely pursued the bandits and captured two of them, namely A Jin and Lu Linyuan, and escorted them to court on the 15th for trial.

Shooting Case in Qiujia'an Qian Binggen, a 41-year-old farmer from Qiujia'an Village in Anshang Township, the Sixth District of Wuyi, was working in the fields the other day when he was shot in the chest by a henchman of Tang in a spiteful act. He was immediately taken to Changzhou Hospital for treatment, but died soon after due to a ruptured heart and lungs.

Jiangyin 72

Yi Zhen Hui Sends Personnel to West Township for Disaster Relief The villages of Ding Taosha and Dingshu in the west of the county have suffered consecutive years of famine. Zhu Xianwen and others requested the Jiangsu Yi Zhen Hui (Charity Relief Association) to provide relief. The Association sent Wei Lengyan to Jiangyin to investigate and confirm the situation. He forwarded the request to the Provincial Government, which approved the allocation of 2,400 relief funds to Jiangyin. The Yi Zhen Hui generously added 600 yuan. On the 14th, it sent Zhang Zhongkuan to Jiangyin to distribute the relief.

Counter-revolutionary Criminal Escorted to County for Interrogation and Detention The Deshun Security Corps of Shazhou discovered counter-revolutionary slogans in Houteng and captured Cai Chengxu, a criminal who committed extortion. He was escorted to the county on the 14th for questioning. The criminal confessed that he joined the Party in January of the 17th year of the Republic through the introduction of Gao Wulaoguan and was responsible for propaganda work. He also confessed to the murder of Xu Xingfu and Xu Bolin. However, he did not admit to posting slogans. After interrogation, he was taken into custody.

County Magistrate Li Orders Investigation into Encroachment on Public Land The Jiangyin Fire Fighting Joint Association of the North Suburbs had a dispute with residents Zha Fuyuan, Ji Xisan, and others over the construction of houses on the site of the former Shuolong Jing'an Palace. The dispute had lasted for ten months. The original site of the Shuolong Palace in Xinheng Street, measuring one fen of land, was owned by the Association and held a certificate numbered Jing 2. It had been encroached upon by Ji Xisan and others who refused to vacate. The other day, the entire association issued flyers to resign. County Magistrate Li read the flyers and, because the matter concerned fire prevention for the entire city, specially ordered Wei Buchan, the district chief of the First District, to investigate and mediate, and summoned Sha Shaoshan of the Joint Association to the government office to explain the importance of the matter. Regarding the encroachment of public land by the Ji family, he ordered that it be handled according to legal procedures and that they not resign.

Zhenjiang 73

Strange News of Impersonating the Chief of the Public Security Bureau A man named Xu Jingzhi, approximately thirty years old, arrived in Zhenjiang last month with Tan Houcheng and Wu Jingming. They stayed at the Da'an Inn on Rixin Street. Xu claimed to be the newly appointed Chief of the Taixing Public Security Bureau, Tan was said to be an aide-de-camp to the Commander-in-Chief of the Nanjing Army, Navy, and Air Force, and Wu was said to be a staff member of the Public Security Bureau. They appeared to be officials preparing to take office. Xu entered the city the other day in the afternoon and went to the Department of Civil Affairs to seek an audience with Director Hu. Director Hu asked his purpose, and Xu said that he was ordered by Commander-in-Chief Chiang to come to Zhenjiang and would be going to take office at the Taixing Public Security Bureau. Director Hu was astonished to hear this, saying that the Chiefs of the Public Security Bureaus of various counties were always appointed by the Department of Civil Affairs and that the Headquarters had never sent anyone, nor had it notified the Department. He asked if he had any official documents from the Headquarters, and Xu immediately produced a document for Hu to see. The gist of the document was that so-and-so was appointed as the Chief of the Public Security Bureau of such-and-such county and was ordered to proceed to take office. The end was stamped with the seal of the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, but there was no supervisor's seal and no proofreading. It was clearly forged. When asked where the document came from, Xu replied that he got it from Tan Houcheng, the aide-de-camp at Headquarters. When asked where Tan was, Xu replied that he came to Zhenjiang with him and was currently staying at the Da'an Inn. After inquiring, Director Hu was extremely surprised and sent Squad Leader Hui of the Provincial Guard with six provincial guards to the Da'an Inn with Xu Jingzhi. Sure enough, there was a person named Tan Houcheng, who was arrested along with Wu Jingming and taken to the Provincial Public Security Bureau. Director Chen interrogated them one by one, and they confessed at length. The general idea was that Xu was obsessed with being an official and was deceived by Tan. The document was given to Xu by Tan, and Tan got it from someone else. The whole thing was repeatedly fabricated and extremely absurd. Someone from Nanjing came today to investigate the matter. It is said that Tan's position as aide-de-camp was also a past fact. Director Chen, because the case involved impersonating an official and forging documents, was not in a position to handle it and has submitted the original confession to the Department of Civil Affairs for review.

County Magistrate of Jintan Accused Yang Zhen, the County Magistrate of Jintan, has been accused of corruption and perversion of justice since taking office last October, and his reputation is terrible. Recently, Jiang Maosong and other citizens of the county submitted a petition to the Provincial Government, requesting his removal and punishment. After receiving the petition, Chairman Ye and Director Hu will send personnel to thoroughly investigate in order to clean up officialdom.

Yangzhou 74

Robbery Case in Mituo Lane The city is not peaceful, and robberies are frequently heard. Yesterday (the 14th) at around 8:00 PM, Zheng Shaoquan's house in Mituo Lane on Caiyi Street in the new city was entered by bandits who spread out to various rooms and ransacked them. It is reported that hundreds of yuan in cash and gold jewelry, totaling nearly a thousand yuan, were lost.

Bandits Rob Qishumiao and Kill a Police Officer Lake bandits are rampant in Qishumiao in this county. Yesterday (the 14th) at around 6:00 PM, bandit boats suddenly arrived, landing with weapons and swarming into the town. They first robbed the police team stationed in the town of six rifles and two box cannons. The town's police team was outnumbered and overwhelmed, resulting in the injury and death of officer Yu Deshui. They then proceeded to rob the town. It was reported to the county by telephone by the team last night.

Bandits Cut and Injure a Victim The home of Xu Zhixiang, a villager from Fan Jingsha Jiaojia Lane in Sanjiangying in this county, was broken into by a bandit in the middle of the night the other day. The bandit, wielding a long knife, slashed Xu's wife repeatedly, causing multiple injuries. She cried for help from her neighbors, and the bandit abandoned the knife and fled.

Nantong 75

Successive Kidnappings in the Countryside Recently, bandits have been active in the countryside of Tong County. Kidnapping and extortion cases have occurred one after another in Xiting, Sanle, Yuxi, and other places. The families of the kidnapped have all received threatening letters, and people are unusually fearful. The Nine County Bandit Suppression Headquarters has dispatched teams to station and secretly investigate the bandits.

Sending Police to Haimen to Escort a Bandit Leader Wu Ziyu, the bandit leader from Dongxiang in Nantong, was captured in Haimen. Upon receiving a telegram from County Magistrate Jiang of Haimen, the County Government dispatched police to Haimen on the 15th to escort him back.

Settlement of the Case of a Police Team Beating a Carriage Owner to Death The Nantong County Police Team, due to a hired car, violently beat Jiang Chuntang, the owner of Lu Shun Carriage, and Jiang died in the hospital at 10:00 PM on the 14th. The carriage industry was extremely angry. After mediation by representatives of various Party and government agencies on the 15th, a peaceful settlement was reached. Team Leader Jin Juechen donated 400 yuan from his salary to handle Jiang's funeral, and another 1,000 yuan in condolences was raised by various circles. The perpetrators, Deputy Team Leader Li Hanbin and police officers Liang Qinghai and Wang Hongchen, were handed over to the County Court for legal punishment.

Court Clerk Sentenced for Fraud Qiu Jizhao and Li Houfu, clerks of the Nantong County Court, used the official seal to commit fraud in the Sanle District. After being discovered by the Public Security Bureau, they were taken to the court. After a trial on the 15th, Qiu and Li were found guilty of two counts of using forged official documents and were each sentenced to two years of imprisonment. They were to serve a combined term of three years and were each deprived of their civil rights for six years.

Pinghu 76

Security Team Continues to Capture Bandits The Provincial Security Team stationed in Xincang Town went to Xima Shenfang in three routes yesterday morning (the 14th) to arrest bandits. They successively captured He Shengrong, Liu Jinyuan, Tao Youfu, Hu Achun, He Xiaohe, and five others, and seized two rifles. However, during the arrest, the villager He Ada was mistakenly shot and killed. The five bandits have now been escorted to Pinghu.

Robbery Case in Shahaixing At Lu Ada's house, a farmer in Shahaixing, about half a li outside the West Gate of Zhapu, six bandits suddenly arrived the other night, broke into the house, tied up Ada and his wife one by one, rummaged through boxes and chests, and robbed them clean. It is estimated that they lost over a hundred yuan in cash, gold jewelry, and clothes.

Huzhou 77

Six Bandits Captured at Tianyunlou The city's Bandit Suppression Headquarters, based on a tip-off this afternoon at around 2:00 PM, reported that several bandits related to a certain case were having tea at Tianyunlou on Zhicheng Road. Upon hearing this, the headquarters dispatched over ten armed soldiers to the second floor of the teahouse, where they found six foreigners sitting at one table. The soldiers first surrounded the six and thoroughly searched their pockets, but found no contraband. The six were taken to the headquarters for questioning.

Hangzhou 78

Civil Affairs and Construction Departments Urge Insect Control In order to prevent and control insect plagues, the Zhejiang Civil Affairs and Construction Departments have issued an outline for the implementation of insect control. Yesterday, they jointly sent a circular telegram to the magistrates of 75 counties, urging insect control personnel to follow the outline, first capturing moths, collecting eggs, and selecting grain seeds, and then continuing to improve rice paddies.

Summer Tax Collection About to Begin The Zhejiang Finance Department has ordered all counties that the collection of summer tax should begin on June 1st. All original land taxes of one tael should be converted to a silver dollar tax of 1.8 yuan. At least 35% of the total annual amount should be collected within four months, with rewards and penalties for surpluses and deficits respectively.

Ferry Industry Dispute Awaits Resolution The Yidu (Charitable Ferry) Office of the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau submitted a report to the Construction Department, stating that the Xiaoshan County Government had included the section from the Qiantang Riverbank to the Xixing Tielingguan into the county road, and all rickshaw donations would be collected by the county, affecting the income of the Yidu. Yesterday, the Department issued an order that all rickshaw donations should continue to be collected by the office as usual until a clear division is determined. As for why Xiaoshan County included it in the county road, it will have to wait until the county responds to resolve this dispute.

Ningbo 79

Robber and Thief Executed by Firing Squad Two robbers and thieves who robbed Yucheng Pawnshop, Zhang Lianhai and Han Baoqing, were escorted to Caoma Road by the headquarters at 11:00 AM yesterday and executed by firing squad. The accomplices, An Dequan, the female offender Zhang Wangshi, and Hong Hushi, were transferred to the court for trial.

Bandits Apprehended at Dadong Inn The Detective Team, based on a secret tip-off, apprehended a bandit named Cheng Anren in Room 31 of the Dadong Inn at the Jiangbei Railway Station last night. They also found two Browning pistols in Room 24 across the street. Xia Xiangshan, the inn's accountant, happened to be staying in that room that night and was also arrested as a suspect.

Shangyu 80

Shocking News of Five Robberies in Songxia The Shouyuantang Pharmacy in Zhangjia Village, Songxia, was suddenly broken into by more than ten robbers in the middle of the night on the 6th. They grabbed an employee and threatened him with a pistol. They robbed over a hundred silver dollars. The bandits then swarmed to the Yitai Chest Shop in the neighboring village of Lu and ransacked it, losing dozens of dollars. Unexpectedly, at one o'clock in the morning on the 7th, a group of bandits returned to Zhangjia Village, smashed the doors of Pan Xiexing Shop, jumped upstairs, threatened them to keep quiet, and used sharp blades to cut open the shop assistants' chests and cages, taking away valuables and silver dollars. Then they went to Zhang Zhiren's house, ransacked boxes and chests, and took everything. Still not satisfied, they broke into Zhang Zhenhe Shop, which was adjacent to Zhang's house, and looted it extensively before leaving with a shout. After the incident, each family checked and found that they had lost more than a thousand taels of silver in total.

Keio University Students Attend Track and Field Competition

Therefore, the Japan Sports Association expressed its deep apologies and decided to request the school to participate because the school's athletes are the best in Japan and are also admired by people across the country. The Japan Sports Association has recently sought the school's consent and has received a reply stating that it will send seven track and field athletes to participate. Important News

Central Asia Survey Team to Mongolia Mining Agreement 108

The Central Asian Survey Team of the American Museum of Natural History in New York had planned to continue excavating ancient animal specimens in Mongolia last year. After repeated negotiations with the Antiquities Preservation Committee on the conditions, the team leader Andes regretted his previous proposal, and the two sides stopped the process. In November last year, Osters, the curator of the Museum of Natural History, sent a letter to the Antiquities Preservation Committee, requesting to continue the investigation in Mongolia this summer. In February of this year, a joint meeting was held, and Osters proved that Andes was commissioned as a representative in the American Science Magazine to publish texts, correcting the previous mistakes, and stating that this trip to Mongolia would be the last time. In the future, the publications and public statements of the Museum of Natural History would no longer contain insulting Chinese words. Therefore, in March, the Antiquities Preservation Committee appointed Ma Heng, director of the Beijing branch, as a representative to sign with Andes in Tuancheng. According to Article 5 of the agreement, "This agreement shall take effect after being approved by the Ministry of Education of the Republic of China." The Antiquities Preservation Committee has reported the situation to the Ministry of Education for approval and filing, and the Ministry of Education has requested the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to issue a license and send it directly to Tuancheng in Beijing for departure. The draft agreement is recorded below: (Draft Agreement between the Antiquities Preservation Committee of the Ministry of Education of the Republic of China and the Central Asia Survey Team of the American Museum of Natural History in New York) Article 1 The Central Asia Survey Team is entrusted by the Antiquities Preservation Committee to investigate in Mongolia. Article 2 The team members are half Chinese and half Western, and each appoints one person as the leader. Article 3 Except for vertebrate animal fossils as stipulated in Article 4, the academic materials collected should all remain in China. Article 4 A. Vertebrate animal fossils collected will be reviewed by a special review committee. Those identified as duplicate specimens or identical to those previously collected will remain in China. B. Those that are different from those previously collected and must be transported to the United States for research may be transported to the United States in moderation, subject to the following conditions: (1) China should send specialized scholars to work together, and all travel expenses and expenses during the research period will be borne by the Museum of Natural History. (2) The American Museum of Natural History should provide the Chinese scholars with the convenience of independent research. (3) After the research is completed, the original objects must be returned to China. Those that must be temporarily retained in the United States for reference should be marked with the words "Antiquities Preservation Committee Depository" when displayed, and two plaster models should be sent to China. Article 5 This agreement shall take effect after being approved by the Ministry of Education of the Republic of China. Article 6 This agreement shall be written in duplicate, with duplicate English translations. Both parties shall each hold an original and a translation. (Signed in Tuancheng, Beijing, March 19th)

Zhejiang Education Department Plans to Popularize Public School Education Plan 110

The Zhejiang Provincial Education Department, in view of the urgent need to popularize adult supplementary education during the period of political tutelage, has drafted a draft plan for public school education in Zhejiang Province. The original plan is divided into: (1) Principles, (2) Organization, (3) Experiment and Guidance, (4) Number of Out-of-School People, (5) Administrative and Teaching Staff, (6) School Buildings and Equipment, (7) Teaching Materials, (8) Budget, (9) Implementation Steps and other nine items. It is heard that this plan will have to wait until the central government officially issues the preliminary plan for adult supplementary education before being revised. The draft plan states that the total number of university students in the province is 10,963,392, requiring 1,540 administrative and guidance personnel and 43,854 teachers each year. There must be 7,309 large and small classrooms, popularized in the Republic of China for 23 years, costing a total of 12,846,782 yuan.

Zhoupu Elementary School in Nanhui County, Jiangsu Province has been established for many years, with many students and outstanding achievements. Review of the Second National Education Conference (13) 112

(4) Design

(1) The Ministry of Education Design Committee shall formulate plans for popularizing education, expanding junior high schools, expanding senior high schools, vocational normal schools, promoting supplementary education, promoting social education, and reorganizing overseas Chinese education groups based on the current situation of overseas Chinese education.

(2) The Ministry of Education Design Committee shall formulate a plan to protect overseas Chinese education based on the attitudes of the governments of overseas Chinese settlements in various places towards overseas Chinese education.

(3) The Ministry of Education Design Committee shall formulate plans for rectifying schools of all levels and types and methods for distributing the overseas Chinese education funds and foundation interest allocated by the National Government.

(4) All plans should widely adopt the opinions of consulate commissioners and overseas Chinese groups and cooperate with education associations.

(5) The Ministry of Education shall formulate all practical, simple, easy-to-implement, and non-conflicting with public law regulations and laws based on the actual situation, opinions of design committees, and overseas Chinese groups.

(5) School Education 113

(1) Establishment of Overseas Chinese Schools (A) The principle is that overseas Chinese run the schools themselves, and they must register with the Ministry of Education; (B) Overseas Chinese can return to China to establish secondary or higher education schools specifically for overseas Chinese children; (C) The Ministry of Education will encourage and subsidize overseas Chinese in establishing schools; (D) The Ministry of Education will selectively establish schools overseas as models for overseas Chinese; (E) Unless under special circumstances and with the permission of the Ministry of Education, overseas Chinese schools shall not receive subsidies from foreign governments and shall not employ foreigners as principals.

(2) Organization of Overseas Chinese Schools (A) Overseas Chinese schools should establish a board of directors. The regulations for the organization shall be prescribed by the Ministry of Education, offering several options for various overseas locations to choose and implement; (B) The board of directors is responsible for raising funds, managing finances, reviewing budgets and final accounts, managing school property, selecting and employing principals, and handling external affairs. The principal is responsible for managing school affairs, employing teachers, and preparing budgets and final accounts. Unless the principal is demonstrably derelict in duty or other unavoidable circumstances occur, neither party may terminate the contract prematurely. The principal may attend board of directors meetings, and individual opinions of board members must be submitted to the board for decision; (C) Overseas Chinese schools should organize faculty and staff associations and may organize student self-governance associations.

(3) Funding of Overseas Chinese Schools (A) Funding standards shall be compiled by the education commissioner of the consulate and the education association; (B) Accounting methods, school property management methods, and economic transparency methods shall generally follow those of domestic primary and secondary schools.

(4) Construction and Equipment of Overseas Chinese Schools Shall use the standards and methods prescribed by the Ministry of Education, but may refer to the standards set by the local government.

(5) Supplementary Items for Moral Education in Overseas Chinese Schools The Ministry of Education shall prescribe general guidelines, and specific moral education matters for each year, month, and week shall be determined locally and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval.

(6) Curriculum and Teaching Materials for Overseas Chinese Schools (A) The curriculum shall be prescribed locally according to the standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education; (B) The Ministry of Education shall prescribe methods for reviewing teaching materials and books, approve existing applicable versions, or provide incentives and set standards, allowing private individuals to edit, review, publish, and award the best materials (C) The Ministry of Education shall entrust experts to edit special teaching materials; (D) Teaching tools, testing methods, and achievement assessment methods shall follow those of domestic schools.

(7) Overseas Chinese School Teachers (A) Consolidate domestic institutions for training overseas Chinese teachers, establish normal schools at home and abroad, or subsidize overseas high schools and normal schools, and entrust them with teacher training; (B) Register teachers. Overseas registration shall be handled by consulates, and domestic registration shall be handled by the educational administrative organs in Shanghai, Nanjing, Guangzhou, Xiamen, and Shantou. The method shall involve reviewing academic records or conducting appropriate examinations, with leniency for current teachers and strictness for those wishing to take up teaching positions. Qualified individuals shall be issued permits; (C) Teachers with misconduct shall have their permits revoked, be dismissed, or be disciplined after returning to China; (D) The Ministry of Education shall order educational institutions in Nanjing, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Xiamen, and Shantou to organize teacher referral agencies to handle referral matters; (E) The Ministry of Education shall set out general guidelines for salary standards and seniority-based pay increases, and submit them to consulates to solicit opinions from overseas Chinese groups and educators before formulating several detailed implementation methods; (F) The Ministry of Education shall establish reward and protection measures, provide bonuses to outstanding teachers, subsidize outstanding domestic teachers to work overseas, and ensure that teachers are not dismissed without cause before returning to China. Teachers shall be hired for a minimum term of two years, with salaries calculated on a twelve-month basis, and transportation and accommodation shall be provided by the school; (G) Further education methods shall be handled in accordance with the regulations for the further education of primary and secondary school teachers and staff in China.

(8) Overseas Chinese School Students (A) Overseas Chinese schools shall set up free places for poor children; (B) The Ministry of Education shall establish regulations for overseas Chinese students returning to China for further education, determine quotas, and provide subsidies; (C) National and provincial schools shall give preferential treatment to poor overseas Chinese students returning to China for education; (D) Overseas consulates and education associations shall handle guidance on further education matters, and domestic educational institutions in Shanghai, Guangzhou, Shantou, Xiamen, and Tianjin shall provide guidance on further education.

(9) Guidance System To be implemented according to the methods prescribed by the Ministry of Education. The main points are: A. The commissioner of the consulate shall be responsible. The commissioner of the consulate must be a graduate of a senior high school or higher normal school with more than five years of education experience, be proficient in both Mandarin and a foreign language, have good character and health, understand the Party's principles, and be familiar with the situation of overseas Chinese. Before being dispatched, they should be trained and practice in guidance work for more than three months by the local educational institutions designated by the Ministry of Education. B. Divide each region into several guidance zones, designate one or two schools in each zone as the center, organize guidance meetings, and plan guidance improvement methods. The central school is responsible for implementation. The central school should unite with the local schools to organize research meetings to study improvement methods and apply joint recreational activities, exhibitions, concerts, and speech meetings. C. Education commissioners and overseas Chinese education associations should often use holidays, weekends, and evenings to organize seminars to assist overseas Chinese school teachers and staff in pursuing their studies. D. The Ministry of Education should regularly send personnel to inspect and guide.

(6) Social Education 114

(1) Remedial Education A. Establish half-day schools, literacy night schools, holiday remedial schools, women's remedial schools, and other institutions. B. Emphasize general subjects such as Party principles, Mandarin, Chinese language, Chinese history and geography, and vocational subjects. The curriculum outline shall be prescribed by the education commissioner of the consulate as needed. C. Funding shall be appropriated from overseas Chinese education funds or raised by the organizers themselves. D. The results shall be assessed by the consulate commissioner and reported to the Ministry of Education. E. Various remedial regulations shall be promulgated by the Ministry of Education.

(2) Social Education Depending on local circumstances, establish popular libraries, reading rooms, popular lecture halls, new drama performance halls, clubs, family improvement associations, and other institutions, under the guidance of local Party committees and education associations. Funding shall be raised by the organizers themselves, with the Party committees and education associations providing appropriate supplementary funds.

(3) Temporary Gatherings Depending on local circumstances, hold annual gatherings for health, Mandarin, education promotion, women's liberation, and family improvement movements, organized by education associations and other institutions.

(4) Various Overseas Chinese Social Education Undertakings Shall be jointly organized by overseas Chinese education groups.

Tenth Implementation of the Mongolian and Tibetan Education Plan 115

(1) Implementation of Educational Administrative Measures

(1) In each league, department, and banner of Mongolia, the respective chiefs shall, under the guidance of the competent educational authorities, organize an educational administrative committee for that league, department, or banner. (2) In each dzong of Tibet and places equivalent to a dzong, the respective chiefs shall, under the guidance of the competent educational authorities, organize an educational administrative committee.

(3) The organizational charter of the Educational Administrative Committee shall be formulated by the Ministry of Education, with the main points being: A. The name of the committee shall be prefixed with the name of the locality; B. A chairman and vice-chairman, one each, and several members shall be appointed by the local chiefs; C. Under the guidance of the competent chiefs, the committee shall be responsible for local educational administrative matters; D. In Mongolian and Tibetan areas where provinces have already been established, the higher-level educational administrative chiefs shall also be responsible for supervision and guidance; E. Expenses shall be paid from local administrative funds.

(4) Educational Administrative Committees in all Mongolian and Tibetan areas shall be established by the end of June 1931, except under special circumstances, and shall be handled by the local chiefs.

(5) The Ministry of Education and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission shall establish a Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui Student Management Committee in the capital to handle matters such as student recruitment, guidance, and the provision of funding. Its organization shall be determined separately.

(6) The government shall establish incentive measures for private individuals who run Mongolian and Tibetan education or compile books and various academic works on Party principles or science in Mongolian and Tibetan languages.

(2) Implementation of General Education Measures 116

(1) In each banner of Mongolia, and each dzong of Tibet and places equivalent to a dzong, primary schools shall be established according to the number of school-age children. At least one shall be established by 1931, and gradually expanded thereafter.

(2) In each league and department of Mongolia and in important locations in Tibet, vocational schools shall be established according to social needs, to be completed within eight years. However, they may be attached to secondary schools or normal schools.

(3) Secondary schools shall be established in Manchuria, Tongliao, Kalaqin Right Banner, Daban, Bandida Temple, Shangdu, Wuyuan, Dingyuan, Jining, Wutubulak, Usu, Changdu, Dazhao, and Dulan, to be completed within six years. First establish junior high schools, and add senior high schools after the fourth year.

(4) Rural normal schools shall be established in Hailar, Taonan, Tumote Left Banner, Sifeng, Duolun, Zhangjiakou, Baotou, Zhungeer Banner, Erqi, Xining, Chenghua, Xinwangfu, Ba'an, Lihua, and Jigu, to be completed within six years.

(5) Mongolian and Tibetan schools shall be established in the capital and Kangding, to be fully established within two years. The existing Peking Mongolian and Tibetan School shall also be strengthened and reorganized. (6) Attention shall be paid to the organization, training, curriculum, and treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan schools. A. The name of the school shall be prefixed with the name of the locality and the name of the banner or dzong. B. Students with equivalent academic qualifications may also be admitted. C. In addition to the nationally unified teaching materials, teaching materials suitable for Mongolian and Tibetan society and textbooks in Mongolian and Tibetan languages combined with Chinese characters shall be added. D. Provide appropriate accommodation, food, and books.

(3) Implementation of Higher Education Measures 117

(1) Earnestly implement the measures for the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students promulgated by the Ministry. During the spring and autumn recruitment periods, the Ministry of Education shall issue a notice to all schools across the country to admit as many Mongolian and Tibetan students as possible, and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission shall inform each league, banner, and dzong to send students to the mainland for education in accordance with the regulations.

(2) National Central University and Peking University should, in accordance with the resolutions of the National Government, open Mongolian and Tibetan classes in the autumn of this year. The recruitment methods shall be drafted by the Ministry of Education and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, and Mongolian and Tibetan areas shall be ordered to guarantee timely delivery.

(3) National universities should establish Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui literature departments or lectureships, but National Central University and Peking University must be established within one year.

(4) Mongolian and Tibetan students who seek advanced academic studies shall, in addition to being admitted to the schools designated in the previous list, be sent to mainland universities or vocational schools for further study in accordance with the regulations on the treatment of Mongolian and Tibetan students. The central government shall allocate funds to subsidize these students.

(5) At an appropriate time, vocational schools or independent colleges or universities for agriculture, industry, and commerce shall be established in suitable locations in Mongolia and Tibet.

(6) Mongolian and Tibetan students shall be sent abroad for further study in installments within six years. The methods are: A. The number of students shall be set at ten for Inner Mongolia, eight for Outer Mongolia, two for Qinghai, eight for Tibet, and four for Xikang, totaling thirty-two. B. The qualifications shall be graduation from senior high school or equivalent academic qualifications. C. The study period shall be limited to three to seven years. Those studying medicine and engineering may be appropriately extended. D. Eight students shall be selected and sent to Japan every two years, and four shall be sent to Europe. E. The study abroad expenses shall be provided by the central government.

(7) Within one year, the Ministry of Education and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission shall draft the organizational charter of the Mongolian and Tibetan Academic Investigation Group, and appoint personnel to conduct the first investigation. The annual funding shall be approximately 10,000 yuan, subsidized by the central government.

Shanghai Schools Support the Recovery of Concession Educational Rights 118

The principals of eleven schools, including Shanghai Special Municipality Qin Yi School, jointly sent a letter to the Chinese members of the Shanghai Municipal Council, requesting assistance in recovering educational rights in the concessions. The letter stated: "To the esteemed Chinese members of the Shanghai Municipal Council, we have read the declaration of the Shanghai Special Municipality Education Bureau on recovering educational rights in the concessions, and have also read the telegrams and letters from all sectors regarding the recovery of educational rights in the Shanghai Special Zone. The arguments are unanimous and heartfelt, and the enthusiasm and determination are admirable. At this time of political tutelage, this proposition is crucial and cannot be delayed. Although our schools are not located in the concessions, we are affiliated with the city's educational services. We feel threatened by the loss of educational rights in the concessions and cannot remain silent. We must speak out. The existence of concessions in our country is a result of unequal treaties. However, concessions are not the same as ceded territories; they are merely residences for foreigners within a certain period. The sovereignty of the owner has not completely disappeared. After reviewing all unequal treaties, there is no special privilege for foreigners to monopolize education. This is an overreach that cannot be justified. This is the first reason why we are eager to recover educational rights in the concessions. The citizens and children in the concessions are mostly educated in an imperialistic manner. Foreigners are anesthetizing our youth, preventing students from enjoying the education of the Three Principles of the People, which is heartbreaking. This is the second reason why we are eager to recover educational rights in the concessions. Before the abolition of unequal treaties and the recovery of concessions, the Shanghai Education Bureau is actively carrying out the movement to recover educational rights in the concessions, preparing for new construction in special zone education, adding as many municipal schools as possible, implementing pre-determined plans, adapting to needs, and refusing to allow concession citizens to be long fooled by the imperialist invasion policy. They are determined to rectify and unify the exclusive educational rights. People share the same mind and reason, so the recovery of educational rights in the concessions is the precursor to the abolition of all unequal treaties and the recovery of concessions. This is the third reason why we are eager to recover educational rights in the concessions. Looking at the four municipal schools in the concessions, new students always lament their lack of opportunities at the beginning of the school year, showing a great scramble. This shows that the enlightened citizens in the concessions, those with spirit, are unwilling to let their children receive a Western slave education and become their tools. Based on the psychology of the citizens, they all yearn for our country's education authorities to recover the monopoly. This is the fourth reason why we are eager to recover educational rights in the concessions. There are many private schools in the concessions that are well-managed, but it is inevitable that some use the name of running a school to make money, even opening two or three pigeon-hole-sized rooms with a school sign hanging outside. The content is not systematic, and in reality, they are gathering places for reactionaries to plot out of bounds, using the concession as a shield. Our country's education authorities have no right to intervene, which is hateful. This is the fifth reason why we are eager to recover educational rights in the concessions. In summary, if we do not recover educational rights in the concessions in the shortest possible time, Shanghai education will forever be a deformed form, not unified and complete. It is the greatest shame in our country's educational history. The esteemed members have high virtue and prestige. This time, being elected as Chinese members is deeply gratifying. We are pleased that the esteemed members are taking office and hope that they will uphold the spirit of fearlessness, urge the Shanghai Municipal Council to wake up as soon as possible, and assist the Municipal Education Bureau in recovering Shanghai's education. The others will sing praises and offer heartfelt prayers to the esteemed members. Yao Wen and others are weak and have little influence, and their words are insignificant. We do not overestimate our ignorance and humbly present our words. We hope you will not disregard them and will carefully consider and await clear instructions. Respectfully wishing you well, Cui Yaowen, principal of Shanghai Special Municipality Qin Yi Elementary School, Huang Junbao of Donggou Elementary School, Sun Shixian, principal of Zhuyin Elementary School, Qu Mingshan, principal of Peiying Elementary School, Gu Zuyu, principal of Zhendong Elementary School, Qu Zhixu, principal of Gaohang Elementary School, Shi Weisheng, principal of Xigou Elementary School, Huang Zuocai, principal of Jingcheng Elementary School, Jin Ming, principal of Wandou Elementary School, Gu Shiqi, principal of Yincun Elementary School, Song Renying, principal of Guangxin Elementary School."

In addition, the Gaohang Education Association and Shanghai Kindergarten Normal School, West District Elementary School, Qinghua Middle and Elementary School, Yucai Middle School, Minfu School, Zhengmeng School, Yafeng Elementary School, Tongcen Elementary School, Wuben East Elementary School, Guocui First Public School, Shangzhi Elementary School, Zhenyuan Elementary School, Qiming Elementary School, Qunyi Girls' School, Doumiye School, Wuxing Middle School, Nanyang Girls' Middle School, Shangde First Elementary School, Shangde Second Elementary School, Shangde Middle School, Fushan School, Yinlou Elementary School, Yafeng School, Huhai School, Yangci Charity School, Youth Middle School, Shanghai Primary Elementary School, Minghui School, North Shanghai Public School, Yangmeng School, and Minli Girls' Middle School, also issued declarations yesterday to support the recovery of educational rights in the concessions.

Private Secondary Schools and Above Abolish Honorary Principals 119

Chen Dewei, Director of the Shanghai Special Municipality Education Bureau, previously requested the Ministry of Education to abolish honorary principals in private secondary schools and above because many of them were irresponsible, leading to the inducement of young people. On the 15th, the Ministry of Education issued an order to all provinces and cities, stating: "According to the report from the Shanghai Special Municipality Education Bureau, some private schools in this city hire social celebrities and contemporary figures to serve as honorary principals. In reality, they never consult on any school affairs. Those who serve as honorary principals are enthusiastic about education and are willing to lend their names to show their support. However, those in charge of school affairs often use their prestige to gain social trust. Therefore, when disputes occur in schools, no one is responsible, making it difficult to handle the matter. The direct victims are the students. The Ministry of Education believes that the system of honorary principals who do not ask about school matters and are not responsible should be abolished to prevent young people from being deceived and to prevent a few scholars from using names to deceive. After investigation, the points raised in the original report are not only true for schools in Shanghai, but also common in other places. In the future, no matter where private secondary schools and above are located, if there is an honorary principal, the position should be abolished to prevent borrowing the name. This order is hereby issued and distributed to all concerned parties and private secondary schools and above in the jurisdiction to comply. This order is hereby issued."

Local News

Wang Rongbao Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 125

Returning to His Post in Tokyo in Three Weeks

Wang Rongbao, the ambassador to Japan, returned to China on the Chichibu Maru mail ship and arrived in Shanghai at 2 PM yesterday. He is staying at the Wengzhou Hotel on Lafayette Road. He is scheduled to go to Beijing within days to report to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on his work in Japan over the past year. Ambassador Wang's return to China is a routine matter once a year and has no special mission. After completing his official duties in Beijing, Wang plans to return to his native Suzhou. He is expected to stay in China for three weeks before returning to his post in Tokyo. There have been rumors that Japan will send troops to China again during the civil war in North and South China. This reporter asked Ambassador Wang about this yesterday. Wang replied that the Japanese government has no such intention. However, there are 300 Japanese soldiers stationed in Tianjin who are now due for rotation, so there has been some slight movement. This has nothing to do with the situation in China. The Japanese government and public opinion both hope that the civil war in China will end soon. The ship on which Ambassador Wang Rongbao returned to China was the Chichibu Maru, a new ship of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company. It arrived in Shanghai on its maiden voyage. It will sail to Hong Kong tomorrow. Because the Chinese ambassador was on board, in accordance with international etiquette, the Chinese flag was hoisted high on the mast of the ship to show respect. Before the Boxer Rebellion in 1900, it was customary to hoist the Chinese flag every time the Chinese ambassador traveled on a foreign mail ship to show respect. After the Boxer Rebellion, this ceremony had long been abandoned. This time, the Chichibu Maru took the opportunity of its maiden voyage to Shanghai, and Ambassador Wang happened to be on board, so it restored the old international etiquette, which is also worthy of commemoration.

Ambassador Wang Rongbao Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

A reporter from the Zhendan News Agency asked Wang yesterday about the mission of his return to China. Wang said, "(1) There are two or three thousand overseas Chinese in Tokyo. Overseas Chinese affairs are managed by the embassy and are quite complicated. If China were to establish a consulate in Tokyo at this time, it would be difficult to raise funds. It is planned to move the Yokohama consulate to Tokyo, but according to the Yokohama consul, although the number of overseas Chinese in Yokohama is not as large as in Tokyo, the assets of overseas Chinese in Yokohama are many times greater than in Tokyo. It is now planned to suggest to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs that an office of the Yokohama consulate be established in Tokyo. (2) To discuss Sino-Japanese cultural affairs. Because the Ministry of Education advocates the recovery of the Japanese Boxer Indemnity, after arriving in Beijing this time, I will contact all parties concerned to negotiate the Japanese refund of the Boxer Indemnity and its use. (3) There is no limit to the number of overseas Chinese going to Japan, and they are often sent back to China by the Japanese authorities, and there is no right to negotiate. It is planned to ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to formulate appropriate measures." In addition, in a conversation at the Wengzhou Hotel yesterday afternoon, he said, "Since the signing of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement, the Japanese government and public opinion have a very good feeling towards our country. However, another group of people expressed dissatisfaction with Shidehara, calling his diplomacy 'diplomacy of inaction' and 'weak diplomacy.' As for the appointment of Shigemitsu as ambassador, I have not heard anything. Recently, our overseas Chinese are often prevented from returning to China. I am planning to contact the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to find a solution. Because in Japan, those with knowledge and assets who go to their country are of course welcome, but those who are destitute and have no knowledge or skills become undesirable elements, which Japan strongly opposes. In my opinion, there is almost no way to negotiate this matter. It is now decided to discuss a solution with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so that in the future, Chinese workers and others who go to Japan must have legitimate purposes and the ability to maintain their livelihoods, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs or a relevant authority will issue them a certificate of departure and notify the Japanese side to allow them to land. This may be possible, and it is also a matter of our country's dignity."

Sino-French Commercial Treaty Signed Last Night 126

Zhang Weihan Will Depart for Yunnan Tomorrow

The Sino-French-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty, which has been under contention for more than a year, was recently finalized after the French envoy Martel arrived in Shanghai and met with Foreign Minister Wang. After days of back-and-forth telegrams, the text of the treaty was drafted. The morning before, Foreign Minister Wang sent Hu Shize, Director of the Asian Department, to Shanghai to meet with Zhang Weihan, the representative of Yunnan, and French envoy Martel for the final consultation. It was decided that the treaty would be formally signed last night at the Nanjing Foreign Affairs Office. French envoy Martel and Zhang Weihan arrived in Beijing yesterday morning. It is also reported that Zhang has already purchased a cabin on the Chichibu Maru, the new Japanese ship making its maiden voyage to Shanghai. After the signing of the treaty, he will return to Shanghai to board the ship, which is scheduled to sail at 10 AM on the 18th at the Huishan Wharf. He will change ships in Hong Kong to return to Yunnan.

National Businessmen's Association Telegraphs for Protection of Commercial Activities 127

Regarding the Zhejiang Provincial Party Department overstepping its authority to reorganize the Businessmen's Association, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday telegraphed to the Central Party Department in Nanjing, the Executive Yuan of the National Government, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, stating, "We have received a letter from the Zhejiang Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce stating that on the 8th of this month (May), we received Instruction No. 148 from the Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee, which stated, 'For compliance, the unified measures for merchant organizations in Zhejiang Province have been issued and implemented by this association, and Wang Zhuzhai, Jin Runquan, and 19 others have been appointed as members of the Zhejiang Provincial Merchant Organization Unification Committee. All merchant groups within the province must immediately cease activities. Therefore, in addition to separate orders, this order is issued to instruct the association to comply, promptly prepare for the conclusion and handover, and await the Provincial Party Unification Committee to receive and handle it.' Upon receiving this order, we immediately convened an executive meeting at 5:00 PM on the 10th of this month and resolved to comply with the Party's order. We also resolved to cease work from the 12th of the same month and await the Provincial Merchant Organization Unification Committee to take over. In addition to submitting reports to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce of the National Government, the Department of Construction of Zhejiang Province, and the Executive Committee of Zhejiang Province, we hereby inform you for your reference.' We have found that the establishment of Provincial Federations of Chambers of Commerce is stipulated in Article 37 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, and the reorganization and responsibility for reorganization are stipulated in Article 42 of the Chamber of Commerce Law and Article 19 of the detailed rules. This instruction from the Executive Committee of the Zhejiang Provincial Party Department not only infringes upon administrative authority but also alters national laws with a provincial Party order, which may obstruct the future of commercial activities. Therefore, we hereby send a telegram to request investigation and correction, and we hope to receive a reply for compliance. Respectfully, Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, Standing Committee Members Su Minsheng, Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangji, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, Peng Chuli, etc. (with seal)."

Yesterday, Five Million Gold Coins Were Not Allowed to Be Exported 128

Reported by the Shanghai Branch of Sumitomo Bank

Intended for Shipment to the United States

Since the rise of gold and the cheapness of silver, large amounts of American silver have been continuously imported into Shanghai. However, the gold coins in Shanghai have been massively purchased and shipped to the United States, and the number has been enormous in the past two months. As a result, the gold coins remaining in Shanghai are only about one-tenth of what they used to be, which will affect the market. Yesterday, a huge amount of gold coins was discovered being prepared for shipment to the United States by customs, and the export was prohibited. The details are recorded below.

Ministry of Finance Prohibits Gold Export: In view of the continuous export of gold coins from Shanghai, with each export amounting to 700,000 to 800,000 yuan, the Ministry of Finance, fearing that it would trigger a financial crisis, ordered the Jianghai Customs to prohibit the declaration and export of gold coins. After receiving the order, the Jianghai Customs issued a notice and informed the local shipping companies that they were not allowed to accept gold coins for shipment to ports in various countries after the ban was issued.

Sumitomo's Shipment Refused: After the ban was issued, the Shanghai branch of Sumitomo Bank suddenly had a large batch of gold coins, amounting to five million yuan (US dollars), yesterday. Because it urgently needed to be shipped to the United States, it intended to declare it for export on the Jackson ship through the American-owned Dalae Bank. All the procedures had been completed, but when it went to collect the bill of lading, it was refused by Dalae, citing the strict ban of the National Government, which made it difficult to handle the shipment. The coins were returned, and as a result, they could not be exported.

Dalae's Freight Loss: The freight for shipping gold from Shanghai to the United States is US$2.5 per thousand yuan. Before the ban was issued in the past two months, the bank's postal ships were used for gold shipments to the United States. Yesterday's refusal to ship the gold coins resulted in a loss of over US$10,000 in freight.

Sharp Drop in Gold Price 129

Lowest Price Reached 502 Taels

24-5 Taels Lower Than the Previous Day

Yesterday, the price of gold in Shanghai suddenly plummeted again. The lowest price in the morning even fell to 502 taels, which was 24-5 taels lower than the closing price of the previous day. As a result, the market suddenly became tense. Foreign goods merchants, who had planned to slightly increase prices due to the sharp rise the previous day, were caught off guard by the sudden decline. In the afternoon, the price slightly rebounded to 508 taels.

Sudden Decrease in Silver Reserves in Shanghai 130

Nearly 2 Million Taels Less Compared to Last Week

A New Record for This Year

According to a survey yesterday, the recent silver reserves in Shanghai suddenly decreased by nearly 2 million taels compared to last week, which is a new record since the silver market crash this year. The reason is the emergency measures implemented by the National Government, such as prohibiting the import of Mexican silver. It is expected that the price of silver will gradually recover in the future.

Hai, Qidong, and Chongming Counties Build Two Warships, Zhen Dong and Zhen Hai 138

To Suppress Pirates

Pirates outside the Wusongkou have become increasingly rampant recently. The people of Haimen, Qidong, and Chongming counties, in view of the weakness of the water police force, jointly raised funds to build two warships to be allocated to the water police for dispatch and to strengthen the force. The people of the three counties jointly elected Gu Nanqun, Dong Diqing, and Mao Liru as members of the preparatory committee to formulate a plan, which was submitted to Zhu Bingzheng, the district chief of the 4th district of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police Corps in Wusong, and forwarded to the Civil Affairs Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government for review. The Provincial Department approved the plan and immediately ordered the Maocheng Machinery Factory in Nanshi, Shanghai, to build the ships. It is now learned that the two warships have been rushed to completion. The cost of each ship is 30,000 yuan. All the equipment, such as rapid-firing guns, machine guns, and steel plates, is in place. The two ships are named "Zhen Dong" and "Zhen Hai." Yesterday, the Maocheng Factory tested the ships, and the results were excellent. The three members, Gu, Dong, and Mao, have submitted a report to the 4th district of the Provincial Water Police Corps and the governments of the three counties, Hai, Qidong, and Chongming, to schedule a joint inspection at the factory and report to the Provincial Department for record.

Tram Strike News 140

Yesterday Morning's General Meeting at the New Station: Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, more than 500 copper workers who drive and sell tickets at the new station gathered at the intersection of Yulin Road and Dalian Bay Road for a general meeting. The negotiating representatives reported on the two negotiations with the police station and the company in the past two days, saying that there were still no results. The capitalists still firmly refused to accept the lowest conditions, such as a uniform wage increase of three yuan for the copper workers, wages during the strike, the release of arrested workers, no dismissal of workers, double wages for Sunday work, and the restoration of jobs for unemployed workers. The crowd at the meeting was extremely indignant and unanimously resolved not to resume work without meeting the lowest conditions. They shouted slogans and paraded around Dalian Bay.

A. The Revolutionary Spirit of Mr. Chen Qimei:

1. Mr. Chen Was a Revolutionary Full of Compromise-Free Spirit: When the Provisional Government of Nanjing Was Established and the Qing Court Sent Representatives South to Negotiate Peace, Mr. Chen Vigorously Opposed the Peace Negotiation Proposition, Insisting on Upholding the Spirit of Non-Compromise and Taking Advantage of This Opportunity to Thoroughly Eliminate the Remnants of the Imperial System, so as to Avoid Endangering the Future. Within the Party, Mr. Chen Especially Advocated Eliminating Evil Thoroughly, Once Saying That to Avoid Defeating the Group, the Harmful Horse Must Be Removed; to Achieve a Change, Changing the String is Valuable. When Dr. Sun Yat-sen Reorganized the Chinese Revolutionary Party After the Failure of the Second Revolution to Concentrate Revolutionary Forces, Mr. Chen Was the Most Powerful.

2. Mr. Chen Was a Revolutionary Who Was Brave to Follow Good Advice and Correct His Mistakes: Since the Assassination of Song Jiaoren and the Failure of the Second Revolution, Mr. Chen Reviewed the Past Failures, All of Which Stemmed From Party Members Not Believing in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Propositions. Therefore, Mr. Chen Advocated That Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Words and Deeds Must Be Absolutely Obeyed, and Mr. Chen Personally Was From Beginning to End an Implementer of the Three Principles of the People.

3. Mr. Chen Was a Revolutionary Who Was Brave in Sacrifice and Most Resilient and Unyielding: He Only Knew That There Was a Party and a Country, and Did Not Know What His Own Life and Death Were Worth. 1. Mr. Chen Was a Revolutionary Pioneer Who Created the Republic of China: The Wuchang Uprising of Xinhai Revolution Had Revolutionary Foundation, but Still Could Not Be Regarded as Solid. However, At That Time, the Rebel Atmosphere Was Rampant, and All Parties Had Extremely Strict Deployments. Shanghai Had a Heavy Garrison. At That Time, Mr. Chen Was Ordered to Punish Yuan. He Did Not Hesitate to Endure Hardships. He First Launched an Uprising in Shanghai, Sending People to Assassinate Zheng Rucheng, the Garrison Commander, and Secretly Ordered the Zhaohao Warship to Launch an Uprising to Promote the Union of Revolutionary Forces in the Southwest, Which Finally Overthrew Yuan Shikai.

C. The Significance of Commemorating Mr. Chen Qimei: Commemorating Mr. Chen Means Emulating His Spirit of Obeying, Obeying Dr. Sun Yat-sen and Abiding by Party Discipline, Emulating His Virtue of Being Brave in Moving to the Good and Correcting Mistakes, and Continuing His Will of Brave Sacrifice, Resilience, and Perseverance.

The Postal Savings Bureau Instructs Its Employees 142

To Be Kind and Humble to Customers

The Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, in order to promote business development, has specially issued instructions to postal savings and remittance personnel in various places, requiring them to be kind and humble to customers. The document states: "The postal savings and remittance business is commercial in nature and is very close to the general public. All staff members in the bureau must be kind, humble, sincere, and thorough to customers. Only then can the public feel convenient, and the business can develop. However, it has been found that among the postal bureaus' savings and remittance staff, there are many who are humble and sincere, but there are also some who are simple, arrogant, and disrespectful. In this situation, not only is it difficult to expand the business and the country suffers endless losses, but the people feel difficulty and society loses the convenience of circulation, which is contrary to the government's intention to reward and encourage savings. Therefore, it is hereby instructed to the various bureaus to instruct their savings and remittance personnel that from now on, they must be humble and sincere to savings and remittance customers and must not be arrogant and disrespectful. The heads of the various bureaus have the responsibility of supervising and inspecting, and they should always check and earnestly handle the matter in order to value their duties."

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce Urges the Submission of Uniform Measurement Procedures 143

The Shanghai Special Municipal Government received a message from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce yesterday, stating: "For the purpose of consultation, Article 6 of the National Uniform Measurement Procedure stipulates that each province, region, and special municipal government should formulate a uniform measurement procedure for the province, region, or special city within six months from the date of implementation of the measurement law and submit it to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review and record. As the Ministry previously ordered that the statutory implementation of the measurement system would be on January 1st of this year, and requested that the city's uniform measurement procedure be formulated and submitted to the Ministry as soon as possible for assessment and record, now that the six-month period is about to expire, the uniform procedures for most provinces and cities have not yet been submitted. It is requested that the previous consultation be reviewed and the project procedure be formulated and sent to the Ministry as soon as possible for review and approval."

Wang Zhou, a Relative of the Victims of the May 30th Incident, Requests That Wang Kuibao Be Reburied in the Public Cemetery 146

The remains of the martyrs who died in the May 30th Incident are planned and managed by the Board of Directors of the May 30th Public Cemetery. More than ten acres of land were purchased at Fangjia Wooden Bridge at the end of Baoxing Road in Zhabei to build a public cemetery for burial, to commemorate their admiration and make them immortal. Yesterday, Wang Zhou, a relative of Wang Kuibao from Changshu, sent a letter to the relatives' association, saying: "Representatives Hu and Chen, my son Wang Kuibao was a car driver during his lifetime. On May 30th, 1925, he participated in the patriotic movement and died for his country at the age of 30. His remains are still temporarily placed in the Tianxia Guild Hall in Zhabei for five years. Although the condolence money of 2,000 yuan has been received, it has slightly eased the injustice. I don't know when the compensation will be resolved, but I have learned that many of the May 30th martyrs are buried in the May 30th Public Cemetery, which is eternal. Because I am an ignorant woman, I temporarily placed him in the Guild Hall, but it is not enough to comfort his heroic soul in the afterlife. Therefore, I have decided to rebury him in the Public Cemetery to comfort his spirit. However, I am an ignorant woman and do not know the reburial procedures. I would like to ask the two representatives to consult with the directors of the May 30th Public Cemetery Association to allow him to be reburied in the Public Cemetery before the 30th of this month, and please inform me of the reburial procedures so that I can follow them. I will be extremely grateful."

Baoming Will Be Powered by Zhabei 149

The Public Utilities Bureau Urges Implementation

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau believes that it is more economical to purchase electricity from large power plants and resell it than for water and electricity plants to generate their own electricity. The first step in its plan to unify the city's power plants is this regulation. In recent years, it has followed this step and made considerable progress. The Zhenru and Xianghua Electric Companies have successively stopped generating electricity and purchase electricity from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company for resale. The Pudong Electric Company has also signed a power supply contract with the China Electric Company and will soon implement it with the China Electric Company's power supply. In addition, there is also the Baoming Electric Company, which is very close to the site of the Zhabei New Power Plant, which is about to be completed and generate electricity. In view of the fact that the company's load has increased recently and the original equipment is insufficient, the Public Utilities Bureau believes that it would be better to stop generating electricity and purchase electricity from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, as the other companies have done. Moreover, the distance is very close, and the line equipment is even simpler. Cooperation between the two parties is beneficial without harm, and the first step in the bureau's plan to unify power plants can be completed. Therefore, it ordered the company to quickly negotiate with the Zhabei Company on power supply methods. It is said that the two companies have negotiated several times on this matter and it is imperative. It should be realized soon.

Notes for Donating to Siam 151

First Submit to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for Approval

Mayor Zhang of the Shanghai Special Municipality, in order to be cautious about donating to Siam, specially instructed the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday: "For your information, we have approved the letter from the Siam Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, which states that the Siamese government has strictly prohibited private organizations or charitable institutions from sending personnel to solicit donations. Please note this and instruct your subordinates to inform them. It is hereby ordered that if any organization or institution intends to send personnel to Siam to solicit donations, it must first submit it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for approval, investigate the international procedures, inform the Siamese government, and obtain a Siamese passport to avoid being detained."

Municipal Executive Committee 156

The Opening of the First District Grain Stabilization Bureau in the County 159

Hours: 8:00 AM to 3:00 PM

Wu Jingqing, the district head of the first district of Shanghai County, convened the local public organizations to establish the Grain Stabilization Bureau, which officially opened yesterday at the Minhang Mass Education Center. Over twenty people attended. Grain stabilization began at 8:00 AM, with the price of each liter of rice set at 240 cash, about 50 cash cheaper than the market price. A total of 400 bags of Min rice were purchased, totaling over 6,670 yuan. In addition to the district's original grain reserve of 2,000 yuan, an additional 4,000 yuan was borrowed from the Pu Hai Bank. All staff members are rotated from various local businesses, with Zhang Jingling, an accountant from the district office, serving as director. There was a considerable crowd of people buying grain. Yesterday, County Head Yan came to Minhang for a sanitation campaign and also visited the bureau.
