Local News Two

Gold High, Silver Low: Pitle Merchants Hit Hard 160

Jia Nong Unable to Pay for Goods

Longmao and Other Foreign Firms File Lawsuits to Recover Losses

Since the phenomenon of gold being expensive and silver being cheap occurred, general import merchants of Pitle (piece goods) have been greatly affected. When they ordered goods from foreign firms, the price of gold had not risen. But when the goods arrived, the price of gold soared, and the interest rate increased accordingly. As a result, the price of goods also increased, and many foreign firms were unable to pay for the goods. Some even ran aground. For example, Jia Nong Foreign Goods Firm previously ordered various piece goods from British firms such as Longmao and Ruikang. Because they were unable to take delivery, they were separately represented by lawyers such as Shen Yuesheng and Jiang Baolian to file lawsuits for damages. The goods ordered by the firm from Longmao included twenty boxes of silk gauze, ten boxes of fancy wool, and thirty boxes of bleached cloth. When the goods arrived in Shanghai, Jia Nong was unable to fulfill the order, and Longmao also paid the customs duties. Now, except for twenty-five boxes of bleached cloth, the remaining goods have been gradually sold by Longmao on its behalf, resulting in a total loss of 5,413 taels, one mace, and one fen of silver. They requested the court to order the owner of the firm, Cheng Jianong and Qin Tingsheng, to repay the money and order them to take the remaining twenty-five boxes of bleached cloth upon payment. As for the goods ordered from Ruikang, there were as many as ninety-five boxes of bi ji and fu chou (types of silk). After Ruikang sold them on its behalf, it suffered a loss of 4,411 taels, two mace, and four fen of silver, and also requested that Cheng Jianong be ordered to repay the money. These two cases were heard by Judge Xu Wenrong yesterday morning. The defendant Cheng Jianong was not present. First, the case filed by Longmao was heard. The plaintiff's lawyer, Shen Yuesheng, stated the type of goods ordered, the actual amount of the loss, and presented evidence such as the order form. In court, Cheng Jianong denied being the owner of Jia Nong Firm. Since there was a question about the subject of the lawsuit, the court ordered the plaintiff to provide evidence. Shen said that the name of the firm was Jia Nong, and Cheng Jianong must have a relationship with it. Also, Cheng's restaurants on Jiangxi Road and the iron factory in Hongkou are all named Jia Nong. The foreign goods firm is actually opened by Cheng. Cheng's lawyer strongly denied it. Shen requested a postponement to gather more evidence and witnesses. Judge Xu approved the request and ordered him to submit a detailed complaint and reschedule the hearing. Then the case filed by Ruikang was heard. It is also necessary to first resolve the issue of the subject of the lawsuit. The plaintiff's lawyer, Jiang Baolian, presented the order form, saying that the writing on the form was personally signed by Cheng Jianong at the plaintiff's foreign firm, which is sufficient to prove that Cheng is the owner of the firm. But according to Qin Tingsheng, the writing on the order form was signed by his son, who is not currently in Shanghai. Judge Xu also ordered the plaintiff to collect evidence and order Qin Tingsheng's son to appear in court and reschedule the hearing.

Police in Two Concessions Arrest Nineteen Major Robbers Yesterday 161

Thirteen Robbers: The Chinese and Western detectives of the Gordon Road Police Station in the Public Concession have been conducting a strict investigation into the case of the robbery of cash at the home of Gu Xuegen in Gujiabang, Changping Road, West Shanghai, on March 31, in which Chinese Constable No. 463 was shot and killed. In order to solve the case as soon as possible, yesterday afternoon at about 5:00 p.m., the head of the Gordon Road Police Station received a tip that the chief robber, Cao Jinbiao, was hiding in the Beijing Apartment at No. 439 Puhai Road in the French Concession. He immediately ordered Chinese and Western detectives, equipped with weapons, to rush to the French Concession Songshan Road Police Station in police cars to meet with the local Chinese and Western detectives and secretly go to the Beijing Apartment. They arrested the robbers Cao Jinbiao, Wu Yi from Jiangbei, 38 years old, Wu Yizhi from Yancheng, 28 years old, Zhou Shudong from Jiangsu, 38 years old, and seven male robbers and two female robbers in Rooms No. 1, No. 3, and No. 24 of the apartment building, a total of thirteen people. They also found a suitcase in Room No. 1 and took it back to the police station. It is said that the robbers hiding in the Beijing Apartment have committed many crimes and are also suspected of being involved in kidnapping cases. It is planned to transfer them to the court for trial today.

Six Robbers: Yesterday morning at about 4:00 a.m., the police in the French Concession received a tip that robbers who had committed medical cases were hiding in a certain house on Route Lafayette in their jurisdiction. They immediately went there secretly and arrested three robbers and brought them back to the police station. According to their confession, there were still accomplices hiding on the front floor of No. 236 Guling Road in the Public Concession. After receiving the confession, the French police immediately sent a letter to the Xinzha Police Station to request detectives to assist in the arrest. Upon hearing the news, the head of the police station ordered detectives to go with them. At about 11:00 a.m. yesterday, the detectives arrived at the entrance of Yulin Lane on Guling Road, where they saw the Zhong Shengtai cigarette and paper shop, which was No. 236. They immediately surrounded the front floor of the building and arrested three male robbers. They also found four live ammunition pistols under the pillows. It is reported that the six robbers who were arrested had committed more than a dozen major robberies in the French Concession. Therefore, the police have locked the robbers in a closed room.

Manager and Foreman of Huasheng Factory Extorted 20,000 Gold by Bandits 162

One of the Bandits Was a Former Employee of the Factory

Rickshaw Driver Wore Steel Armor

Represented the Owner to Negotiate

Detectives Ambushed and Captured Five Bandits

Cao Yugui and Qi Youcai, the managers of Huasheng Electrical Appliance Factory at No. 2865 Zhoujiazui Road, and Ren Hongcai, the foreman, have been receiving threatening letters since the 3rd of this month, demanding 20,000 yuan. They also agreed to meet at the Bazihui Bridge near the Xin Xin Factory on Baoxing Road in Zhabei. The person who went should hang a vegetable basket on the rickshaw as a sign. A few days ago, Cao and others sent Liu Xiaocai in a rickshaw to meet Xue San and Zuo Qijun from Jiangbei. They started negotiations. Yuan Asan, Liu's rickshaw driver, interjected and said that Huasheng Factory's business has been poor recently and the amount demanded is too extravagant. If it were a few hundred yuan, it could be given to the manufacturer. At that time, Xue and Zuo were very dissatisfied and pulled out their guns, saying to Yuan that at least 10,000 yuan was required, otherwise they would destroy the factory and kill people. They told Liu and Yuan to go back and figure out a way, and they would reply at the same place at 7:00 p.m. on the 14th. After Liu and others returned, they told Cao and others, who reported to the Yangshupu Police Station. Detective Su Changsheng, Detective Su Yinggen, and Detective Li Pengfei rushed to Bazihui Bridge at that time and ambushed nearby. Liu and Yuan were still in contact with the bandits. Yuan was ordered to carry a paper bag, with only 25 yuan in it as a token, but the inside was waste paper. At first, Yuan was afraid of being detected by the bandits and being shot. The detectives gave him a piece of steel armor to wear inside his clothes. Yuan suddenly became brave and went forward. Seeing that the person who came was Xue San, he handed over the paper bag. Xue asked how much was in the bag. Yuan replied that it was only 500 gold. Xue thought it was too little and said that it had to be 5,000 yuan. Yuan asked him to accept it first and the rest would be raised later. Xue accepted it and turned to leave. The detectives who were ambushing in the four corners quickly rushed up and surrounded Xue. Xue tried to escape and was shot in the foot by the detectives before he was arrested. Four accomplices, Zuo Qijun, Lu Xiuqing, Sun Sankai, and Zhou Shuli, were arrested in the area. They then went to No. 1402 Dongjiaxing Road, the bandits' den, and searched it, and arrested a bandit woman, Wu Zhangshi (aka Xu Zhangshi). Except for Xue, who was sent to the hospital for treatment, the rest were taken back to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Feng Shide interrogated them. The plaintiffs, Zeng Yugui and others, proved that they had repeatedly received four threatening letters and the process of sending Liu and Yuan to contact the bandits. When asked about the defendant Zuo Qijun, he admitted that he wrote the letter, but the matter was initiated by Xue and Lu. Lu Xiuqing confessed that he used to work in the Huasheng Factory, but was laid off in August of the previous year. He is now pulling a rickshaw for a living. Xue San said that the manager of the factory, Ye Youcai's house, was robbed on the 30th of last month and received a threatening letter demanding 300 yuan. Xue wanted to imitate this act and asked Zuo to write a letter. Sun Sankai confessed that he was invited by Lu to go to Bazihui Bridge, saying that he was asking people for money. Zhou Shuli confessed that he was invited by Xue San to help him. Wu Zhangshi confessed that she worked in a yarn factory and knew nothing about this matter. There were no firearms in her house. The court ordered the defendants to be detained for a future hearing.

American Abuses Hired Chinese Woman 163

Working Twenty Hours a Day

Beaten with Fists and Feet

Chinese Consul Requests Shi Heshi to Sign a Written Statement

World News Agency, San Francisco: An American named Shi Heshi, who has worked for the Shanghai Concession Electric Company for a long time, returned to the United States with his family on the President Taft, accompanied by Zhang Yafeng, a 38-year-old woman from Sichuan. According to Yafeng, she started working on the 26th of last month. At that time, she was unwilling to travel to the United States. Shi Heshi said that if she was unwilling to go to the United States, she could only hold the child and send it off the ship. However, after boarding the ship, she was forbidden to leave. On the ship, she took care of his wife and children, washing and other things, working every day from 4:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m., sometimes beaten with fists and feet. The passengers on the ship sighed that the abuse was too excessive and said that he must be forbidden to go with her and sent back to Shanghai to avoid mistreatment. At that time, someone called the Chinese Consulate General to request intervention. Consul General Zhang was away on business, and Zhang Zichang, the consular assistant, went to the ship. According to Shi Heshi, he had agreed to pay 50 yuan per month in Shanghai currency, and there was a deposit in the American Consulate. Yafeng said that the wages were indeed received by her husband, but she did not dare to disclose the abuse and said that she was willing to work as a maid. Zhang Zichang then requested Shi Heshi to sign a written statement, stipulating that Zhang Yafeng would be in the United States for a maximum of six months, and Shi Heshi's friend in this port would also sign, guaranteeing that there would be no more abuse in the future.

Young Man, Troubled by Livelihood, Commits Suicide by Poisoning Due to Despair of the World 164

Three Injections of Cardiac Stimulants

Still Not Out of Danger

Lu Mingzhong, 25 years old, from Changzhou, lived near Huayuan Stone Bridge, Lan Ni Du, Pudong. He worked in the Nanhua Printing Office on Taopeng Road, Puxi, earning about 30 yuan per month. With a family of several people, at this time of expensive rice and firewood, the wages he earned were difficult to maintain the livelihood of the family, resulting in a high debt and no way to cope. He suddenly had the idea of being tired of the world. Yesterday at noon, he wrote two suicide notes at home, one to his mother and one to his cousin, and secretly took sleeping pills to commit suicide. At 2:00 p.m., the poison took effect and he fell on the bed, unable to speak. His family noticed and rushed to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. The doctor found that Lu's pupils had stopped and his pulse was sinking. He immediately gave three injections of cardiac stimulants, which slightly turned the tide. At 8:00 p.m., he was still not out of danger.

23.2 Miles Per Gallon of Gasoline

The various cars produced by the American General Motors Manufacturing Plant have always been highly regarded, especially the Chevrolet car, which is popular in the world. Mr. Vctior N. On the spot, there were various performances of Chevrolet's fuel-saving and strong body. Yesterday afternoon, the reporter of this newspaper was also invited to test ride. First, the firm cut off the gasoline in the car and added a glass container to the car, injecting a quarter of a gallon of gasoline, and using a leather tube to introduce the oil into the engine. Mr. De Frack personally drove it, speeding between Daxi Road, Haige Road, and Xiafei Road, traveling 5.8 miles before using up a quarter of a gallon of gasoline. Based on this calculation, Chevrolet cars can travel 23.2 miles per gallon of gasoline, making it the most fuel-efficient car. Liu Caisheng Acquitted in Extortion Case 172

Cao Xiaolong, along with the woman Tan Tingjin, the former accuser Zhang A'san (also known as Su Yongchang), Li Jinbiao, Liu Caisheng, and the woman Wang A'feng, etc., illegally detained Tan Tingjin at No. 16 Moulin Street, Avenue Joffre, in the French Concession, attempting to extort 5,000 yuan in foreign currency. The police arrested Zhang Su and brought him to the Special District Local Court. Liu Caisheng was released on bail after questioning, while the others were detained for further investigation, as previously reported. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi continued the joint hearing. The two defendants, Zhang and Wang, hired lawyer Fan Gang, while Liu hired lawyers Wang Fuchang and others to defend them in court. First, the police lawyers, Ru Baoyi, Wang, and Yaotang, stood up and requested the withdrawal of the charges against Liu Caisheng, because the police investigation showed that Liu was not involved in the case. Judge Wu stated that according to Article 264 of the criminal law, withdrawal of a complaint should be made before the start of the first instance trial. Since the trial was already in progress, it should await legal judgment. The request of the police was therefore denied. The police lawyers then further explained the difficulties of the police in handling cases and the reasons for requesting the withdrawal of the complaint after the case was submitted. They said that the police should abide by the agreement for criminal defendants, and submit the case within 24 hours after the arrest. They did not have sufficient time to conduct a detailed investigation like the domestic judicial authorities. Therefore, the usual practice was to submit the defendant within a definite period to comply with the agreement, and then conduct further investigation. If it was found that the defendant had not committed a crime, even if the trial was in progress, they could request the withdrawal of the complaint. If it was believed that since the trial had already begun, the withdrawal could not be made halfway, and it must wait for the judgment, the law would certainly be so, but the defendant would inevitably suffer unnecessary harm. In order to avoid this kind of suffering for the defendant, they should act according to previous practice. Liu Caisheng's lawyers, Wang Fuchang and others, seeing that the court did not grant the police's request, stood up and requested that the part concerning Liu Caisheng be debated first, citing precedent. The court approved it. The lawyers made their arguments, and Judge Wu announced the verdict that Liu Caisheng was innocent and released. Then the other defendants were interrogated again, and the result was that they were still remanded in custody separately, and the hearing was continued to a later date.

Former Concubine's Lawsuit for Money 173

Zhang Decai, residing at No. 808 Xiang Kang Lane, Baker Road, works as a clerk for a foreign firm, earning more than one hundred yuan a month. He is not yet thirty, but already has three wives and concubines. His third concubine, Wang Jin'e, is twenty-four years old and has been freely associated with Zhang for three years, having one child, also three years old. She is currently pregnant. They first built a golden house in the north of the Huangpu River, and then moved to No. 812 1/2 Xiang Kang Lane. The three wives and concubines lived in the same lane. Unexpectedly, on March 10th of this year, Zhang and Wang Jin'e developed animosity, and both wanted to separate. They went to a certain hotel and wrote a separation agreement, each holding a copy. There were no witnesses at the time of the agreement. Afterwards, Wang Jin'e claimed that in addition to the separation agreement, Zhang had also given her a note promising to pay 1,600 yuan. She hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the Special District Local Court, requesting an order to pay 1,600 yuan in foreign currency. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong opened the court. The plaintiff, Wang Jin'e, explained the situation and submitted the note as evidence. She also invited the landlady of the second landlord, Zhu Li, to testify, who claimed to have heard Wang asking Zhang for money, but did not know what kind of money she was asking for. Zhang denied having written the note. Both lawyers debated to the end. Judge Xu ordered both parties to wait for the verdict on the morning of the 21st of this month.

Why are There So Many Lawsuits for Divorce? 174

Ma Tongli Sues Wife

Ma Tongli, a resident of this county, recently sued his wife, Ma Ma'shi, in the local court, claiming that she was unchaste and dared to run away with his belongings. He stated that he could not live with her anymore and requested a divorce. His statement was roughly as follows: The plaintiff is thirty years old this year, living at No. 27 He Kang Lane, Nine Acres. On February 1st of the 17th year of the Republic of China, he married the defendant, Ma Ma'shi, through a matchmaker. They have not had any children. However, the defendant is unusually fierce, often going out, even staying out overnight. On July 17th of last year, after being reprimanded by the defendant's aunt, she falsely accused the plaintiff of beating her and filed a lawsuit. The court sentenced him, but he was acquitted on appeal. Since then, the defendant has disappeared without returning. He searched repeatedly without success. Therefore, starting from March 16th of this year, he published advertisements in various newspapers, such as Shen Xinmin, calling for her to return quickly, but still there was no news. The defendant had falsely accused him, and the plaintiff was almost criminally punished. It is clear that the defendant has inflicted a serious insult on the plaintiff, and the affection has been severed. This is one reason for divorce. Not having offspring is the greatest form of unfilial piety. Since marrying, there have been no children. Letting her leave without a trace will leave the plaintiff a widower for a long time, worried like Bo Dao. This is not fair. This is the second reason for divorce. When the defendant ran away, she took everything, showing that she had no intention of returning. This is the third reason for divorce. Therefore, he filed this lawsuit, requesting permission for divorce. The defendant stated in the criminal lawsuit against the plaintiff that she lived at No. 140 Mao De Lane, Binlang Road, Little Sandu. Now that she is gone without a trace, he requests a public announcement for service of process. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00, Judge Yang Keqian specially opened the Sixth Tribunal to hear the case. The plaintiff arrived in court with his lawyer, Shen Yong. Since the defendant's address was unknown, a special representative lawyer, Ren Enji, appeared in court to present her case. The judge questioned the plaintiff, Ma Tongli, who stated the previous circumstances and presented the published advertisements as evidence for the court's inspection. The judge then invited the prosecutor, Xu, to the court to express his opinion. After the lawyers Shen and Ren debated each other, the judge announced the end of the debate and scheduled the verdict for the morning of the 19th of this month. Then the court adjourned.

Shi Erlang Sues Her Husband

Shi Erlang, a woman from Chongming, recently hired lawyer Gong Yingxuan to sue her husband, Yang Quanlang, in the local court, claiming that he had seduced and then abandoned her, and requested a divorce. She stated that she was originally the wife of Huang Zhiwen, but unfortunately her husband died in the 14th year of the Republic of China. Then, through the matchmaker Chen Dashu, she remarried to Yang Quanlang. It was only after she married him that she learned that the defendant still had a wife. She regretted it. Recently, she has been subjected to abuse and abandonment. Therefore, she wants to separate from him. The defendant, Yang Quanlang, also hired lawyer Gong Tongyuan to file a counterclaim, claiming that Shi Erlang, under the instigation of an adulterer, falsely sued for divorce. He filed a counterclaim, requesting that she be ordered to live with him and to recover the silver and clothing that she had taken. He also claimed that he married Shi Erlang as a concubine in the 15th year of the Republic of China through a matchmaker. For the first five years, the relationship was quite good, so he opened an oil shop in the South City and let her manage the money. Later, because Shi Erlang secretly had an affair with Zhou Chengzhang, the love between the couple broke down. Due to the importance of face, he tolerated it. On February 27th of this year, she was again instigated by the adulterer Zhou Chengzhang and took more than 500 yuan in cash and jewelry from the shop, leaving nothing behind. Therefore, he published a warning in the newspaper and filed a lawsuit in the prosecutor's office of the court, requesting that the plaintiff's lawsuit be rejected and that she be ordered to live with him. Yesterday, Judge Du Xian opened the court for hearing. Both parties and their lawyers stated their cases. The judge tried to reconcile them, but neither side agreed. After the debate began, he announced the end and scheduled the verdict for the 17th (today).

Husband Denies Wife and Child; Wife Requests Blood Test to Prove Paternity 175

Conclusion of Hearing on Abandonment of Wife Case

Verdict Scheduled for the 21st

Gao Fengshi (age 43), a woman from Changshu, and her son Gao Xiangcheng (age 20) sued her husband Gao Songlin in the local court, claiming that he had abandoned them and requested to live with him. Their complaint stated that when the plaintiff was 21 years old, her younger brother opened a bamboo weaving shop in Jin Sheng Lane behind the New Yamen (i.e., the Special District Court). At that time, there was a man named Wu A'er who also lived in Jin Sheng Lane. The defendant, Gao Songlin, was friends with Wu and very close to him. Therefore, Gao often went to Wu's place to play and chat. That's how the plaintiff got to know the defendant. Then he asked Lu Jie, Wu A'er to be matchmakers, and came to her house saying that his wife had died and that he wanted to remarry the plaintiff as his wife. They got married that year and lived together at No. 10 Gongyi Old Factory, Caojiadu (because the defendant was from Caojiadu). They lived together for more than a year and then moved back to the defendant's house. Only then did she realize that the defendant still had a first wife. But what's done is done, and she had to blame herself. She lived with the first wife for three years. Because she was abused by the first wife, she moved to Nanchang Fen Lane in Shanghai and lived with the defendant for about four years. They then moved to No. 107 Beilong, Shunjin Lane, Hongzhen. Since last year, the defendant has not come often and has not cared about the daily expenses. She has not been paid any attention. Therefore, she filed this lawsuit, requesting to live with him. The case was opened for hearing but not concluded. Yesterday, Judge Du opened the court again for a continued hearing. The defendant hired lawyer Liu Huihuang to defend him. The plaintiff Gao Fengshi and her son Gao Xiangcheng arrived in court, recounting the previous situation. When asked, the defendant Gao Songlin stated that he was 55 years old and from Caojiadu. He denied that the plaintiff was his wife and said that his father had a grocery store when he was alive. The plaintiff was a neighbor and often came to the store to buy things. That's how they met. They talked and joked, that was true, but there was no cohabitation. Gao Yang, 57 years old, also testified, saying that Gao Songlin was her husband and lived in Gao's house in Caojiadu. Her husband did not take a concubine. At this point, the plaintiff interrupted and said that when she married him, it was said to be a replacement wife. Moreover, her son, Xiangcheng, was indeed born to Gao Songlin. If the court did not believe her, they could do a blood test. She asked the court to examine Xiangcheng's face to see if it was the same as the defendant's. The judge understood the situation and announced the end of the debate, scheduling the verdict for the 21st of this month.

Husband Has Another Lover; Wife Commits Suicide in Anger by Taking Poison 176

Bottle of Lysol

Life is in Great Danger

The North Station Grand Hotel at No. 5 Jielu, North Railway Station, had a male and female passenger from Fujian last month, carrying several pieces of luggage. They were led into room number 20 by the tea boy. The registration book showed Gu Jinfu, age 24, and Ms. Gu, age 21, both from Fujian. They had been staying at the hotel for more than a month. They often went out hand in hand, showing great affection. Two days ago, Gu Jinfu went out and did not return. Only Ms. Gu was in the room. Yesterday morning around ten o'clock, Ms. Gu went out alone. Not long after, she returned to the hotel. At three o'clock in the afternoon, she rang the bell and told the tea boy that she was not feeling well today and needed some tea to drink. The tea boy went out and brought boiling tea into the room. He caught sight of her lying on the bed, her face pale. He called out to her, but she did not respond. He immediately reported to the accounting office and hired a car to take her to Tongren Hospital for treatment. When she arrived at the hospital, she was already delirious and unable to speak. After the doctor gave her an injection and medicine, she gradually woke up. It was discovered that she had taken "Lysol". She was transferred to Guangren Hospital. Because she had taken too much poison, her life was in danger. According to the investigation, Ms. Gu took the poison because her husband Jinfu had another lover. It's truly tragic.

Fear of Trouble; Moving the Corpse 177

Jin Chongxuan Dies by Hanging

Zhou Peiyin Fears Being Implicated

Jin Chongxuan, 36 years old, from Yongjia, Wenzhou, Zhejiang, had been unemployed for a long time. He came to Shanghai to make a living. His younger brother, Jin Chongwen, was a boatman. After Chongxuan arrived in Shanghai, he stayed with his brother's friend, Zhou Peiyin. Zhou lived at No. 179 Huining Road, near the Xin Puyu Hall in the South City. He ran a wood shop called Zhou Changfeng Woodworks. Because Jin had no job in Shanghai to support himself, he obtained a permit to live as a peddler. However, he was unfamiliar with the area and had few customers. He also suffered from a severe illness and could not eat. He could only eat two buns a day. Although he was hungry, he could not swallow. He could only blame himself and could not find a way out. So, the night before, he hanged himself in his residence to end his life. Zhou, fearing being implicated, carried the body to the gate of Xu Shuncheng Copperworks at No. 250 behind the vocational school and hung it on the door, making it look like he had died outside. Yesterday morning, Xu Shuncheng's partner discovered the body and was shocked. He fell to the ground and could not speak for a long time. After being awakened by his companions, he told them to look. They were all alarmed and notified the police. The police inspected the way the deceased was hanged and determined that he had not died there. They investigated and found out the truth. Zhou's wife, Zhou Wangshi, was detained and interrogated at the Second Precinct's Second Substation. The neighborhood chief, Gu Tiyun, from the 25th Bao and 12th Tu was ordered to report to the local court for an inquest. Prosecutor Yang and the coroner arrived at the scene. They found that the deceased had indeed died by hanging. They ordered the family to collect the body and await further instructions.

Human Traffickers Abduct Five Children One After Another 178

Three Traffickers Sentenced to Jail as a Warning

Tang Zhangshi, a woman from Ningbo, 24 years old, twice abducted children on the 21st and 25th of last month. The first was Li Xiaomao, a 6-year-old boy from the home of Li Baishi, a Ningbo woman, at No. 61 Yongyu Lane, Beller Road, in the French Concession. The others were Qiuhe, a 10-year-old girl from the home of Yuan Qitao, a Songjiang man, at No. 206 Route Say Zou-Ling, along with Tianru, a 6-year-old boy, and Tianshun, a 10-month-old boy (carried out by Qiuhe). The last was Juhua, a 9-year-old girl from the home of Zhang Shiyong at No. 209 on the same street. She colluded with Wang Menghong and his wife, who were vendors on the Xin Ningxing steamship, and asked someone to take the children to Ningbo. The first child, Li Xiaomao, was sold to Wang Aigui's family in Jiangbei for 80 yuan to be their son. The remaining four children were taken to Fushi Pavilion and sold to Wang A'mei's family in the countryside. While they were negotiating the price, the French Concession detectives Cao Anchang and Bao Hangguangfu discovered the situation and arrested Tang Zhangshi and Wang Menghong, as well as Wang Maoshi, who was involved. They were taken to the police station. Then they went to Jiangbei, Fushi Pavilion, and other places in Ningbo to retrieve all five children and bring them back to Shanghai. The French Concession police first returned them to their families. Yesterday, Zhangshi and others were sent to the French Court for investigation. Each plaintiff reported the previous situation, saying that the children were watching a funeral procession in front of the door when they were abducted. They requested a strict investigation. Tang Zhangshi confessed to abducting the children and receiving 80 yuan for Li Xiaomao. The woman shared 39 yuan, and the rest was shared by Wang Menghong and others. Wang Menghong stated that Zhangshi gave the five children to the wife of a civilian to sell in Ningbo. Afterwards, the civilian received 15 yuan. He did not know where his wife had fled. Wang Maoshi stated that Wang Menghong was the woman's younger uncle. Although the woman also shared 15 yuan in this abduction, she was not present at the time and asked for leniency. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Tang Zhangshi to four years in the women's prison, after which she would be expelled from the French Concession. Tang Zhangshi's four-year-old daughter, Liu Peng, would be sent to the Jiliang Institute to be raised. Wang Menghong was sentenced to one year in the Western prison. Wang Maoshi was sentenced to one month as a warning.

Ninth District Party Headquarters 184

Requests Punishment for the Head of the Fourth Precinct of the Third District

For Interfering with the Farmers' Harvest in Laoshu Sha

The Ninth District Party Headquarters of this city stated that the Asian Petroleum Company, a foreign merchant, had purchased a large number of farmland in Laoshu Sha, Gaogiao, and converted them into oil pools. After several negotiations, it was agreed that the farmers would be allowed to harvest the crops planted in the fields. Now that it is time to harvest the crops, the head of the Fourth Precinct of the Third District, Lan, suddenly led armed police to interfere and confiscated many farming tools, and arrested four farmers. After hearing the news, the headquarters submitted a report to the Municipal Executive Committee yesterday, requesting that the Municipal Government be consulted to negotiate this case and punish the head of the Fourth Precinct of the Third District. They also requested that the report be forwarded to the National Government, stating that in the future, if domestic landowners discover land leases or disguised private sales, they should pay 80 to 90 percent of the income as tax, in order to prevent the spread of foreign economic power in the interior and to develop all production enterprises in our country, so as to meet the needs of social livelihood and avoid the phenomenon of surplus industrial and commercial goods while the necessary living goods are reduced.

Carelessness on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Train 188

At 6:45 yesterday morning, the first express train from Zhabei on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway arrived at the South Station. At 1:05 in the afternoon, one of the cars in the train, a 168 third-class passenger car, suddenly caught fire. Because the weather was dry and windy, the fire was fierce. The stationmaster immediately ordered the railway police officers stationed at the station, Cai Qingquan and Zhu Hongfei, to cooperate with the station staff to board the car and try to put out the fire. The fire was quickly extinguished. The cause of the fire was sparks from the engine's coal fire that flew onto the roof of the car. The car was uncoupled and sent to the factory for repairs.

A Laughing Matter Hai Ke 196

Bride: Darling, I want you to set up a little garden in the open space behind the house.

Groom: Are you planning to plant flowers?

Bride: No. I bought a batch of bird seeds. I want to grow a few thrushes to play with.

Father: Child, you must know that politeness is the most important thing in life. It's always good to be polite to people outside. It's good in that it doesn't cost you anything.

Son: Father's words are good. So, if I have something important to telegraph to a friend, should I add "Respected Brother So-and-So, Your Excellency," "Your humble brother So-and-So bows and salutes" on it?

Manager: I originally wanted to hire a salesman here, but he must be familiar with the situation on the market to be qualified.

Applicant: Sir, I couldn't be more familiar with the situation on the market. I know exactly where it's lively and there are lots of cars and horses, and where it's desolate and you'll run into a pig butcher.

A: I heard that Lao Bing is engaged in the chicken farming business. I wonder how he's doing.

B: He's doing extremely well. The hens he raises are all self-sufficient, which saves him a lot of money.

A: How can chickens be said to be self-sufficient?

B: They lay eggs and eat them themselves to fill their stomachs, without relying on the owner to feed them. Isn't that self-sufficiency?

Farewell Chronicle of the Chinese Athletes' Delegation in Two Days 197

— Huang Jiping

The Far Eastern Games, which contain a non-military international war, will be held in Tokyo on the 26th of this month. Our country has carefully selected more than 130 athletes to go abroad for the expedition. This feat has already caused a sensation across the country. The weight of the mission the athletes bear and the eagerness of the people of the country are self-evident. The farewell party held by 24 Shanghai organizations on the 8th floor of the Hua'an Building on the 13th and the send-off at the Wusong Wharf yesterday truly represent the enthusiastic mood of the entire nation. I have excerpted the trivial matters of those two days and briefly written them to tell the readers of Free Talk.

On the 13th, the reception at the venue, such as Huang Jingwan and Zhu Shaoping, were busy arranging the venue in an orderly manner. After 2:00 PM, more than 100 male and female athletes arrived one after another, full of energy, worthy of the true color of Chinese athletes. It is a pity that the once famous Sun Guiyun did not come, and Zhao Dexin was absent due to serious illness. The eccentric Liu Changchun勉强 (mian qiang - did with effort) attended with a limping foot. It is said that the foot injury will be difficult to recover for a while, which seems worrying. The highly respected old man Ma Xiangbo, who is in his nineties, also came with a cane. This old man is really in high spirits. After a group photo at half past two, the guests and hosts took their seats and held a ceremony. The speeches of all the guests contained profound meaning and did not involve the bad habit of flattery. Chen Dezhen's opening speech was based on the benevolent intention of "a gentleman loves others with virtue," with a tone of advice and warning. He opposed others blindly praising the scene and hoped that the athletes would pay attention to hygiene and behavior, and take into account the face and glory of the country in everything. Ma Xianglao's speech, looking back on the past and present, was extremely sad. He said that the current situation in China is because we have lost our duty as masters. Chinese people like to talk about appearances. He remembered when Yuan Shikai was in power, he was told how well the police in Beijing were managed, boasting that they were not inferior to foreigners. He replied that the appearance was the same, but the substance was still lacking. Yuan did not like to hear this. He hoped that the athletes would pay attention. He also said that the Japanese are insidious and cunning. In the past, there was Huo Yuanjia, who had extraordinary strength. The strongmen of various countries were not his opponents. Later, he was envied by the Japanese, and as a result, he died of poisoning. The old man saw through his treachery, and the listeners were furious. The physical educationist Wu Yunrui said that our country's athletes are not lacking in physical strength, but the methods are not good. The best thing to do on this trip is to capture their sports posture and use it as a model after returning. Liu Jinzhu said that the Japanese despise our compatriots and even insult us with inferior nationalities. When you are in the East, you should pay attention to hygiene everywhere and do not speak loudly or shout strangely. Even if you encounter unfairness during the competition, do not resort to violence. He described the Japanese's malicious conspiracies to the fullest. Finally, Lu Ming, on behalf of the athletes' delegation, accepted the yellow silk flag "Our Martial Arts Promote" presented by the 24 organizations, and replied on behalf of them. His words were very appropriate. His general idea was that the schools have the name of physical education guidance but no actual guidance. Many people put the responsibility of sports on a few athletes and do not have a comprehensive plan. They treat athletes as a special class, which is tantamount to severely criticizing those who misunderstand physical education. Finally, the guests and hosts bowed to each other and dispersed.

On the 15th, the weather was clear and a gentle breeze was blowing. At 7:00 AM, the Wusong Wharf was already crowded with people, and the traffic in front of the gate was heavy and could not be squeezed out. The Chinese athletes arrived one after another after 8:00 AM. The men and women were all beaming and full of energy. The photographers from various newspapers were busy and overwhelmed. Huang Jingwan called himself the director, and the reporters benefited greatly from his assistance. Sun Guiyun was most afraid of people taking pictures of her, but the reporters all wanted to try it. According to her, she had a total of forty or fifty pictures taken of her in the morning. Li Xinghua and Li Mudan also had many pictures taken. Professor Bu Qi (transliteration) and his wife from Northeast University were also very eye-catching. They are both physical educationists and newly married. They took the opportunity to spend their honeymoon. The new couple frequently comforted the Northeast athletes. When she was photographed, she was embarrassed. Bu Qi was very straightforward and insisted on taking a picture with his wife. The two of them pulled and held each other, and the audience laughed. Zhang Boling is the general representative of the Chinese team. As soon as he arrived at the port, the people who came to see him off were eager to shake hands with him. He seemed to be very afraid of trouble, so he ran to the highest floor of the ship and chatted with the captain and first officer. Hao Boyang arrived late as the host. Many Chinese and foreigners were looking for him to talk to him. He shuttled through the crowd, with a smile on his face. A certain girls' school and a certain chamber of commerce in Japan presented two commemorative flags, embroidered with "Great China" and other words. Representative Hao accepted them happily on behalf of the entire group. At 9:30, more and more people came. The sound of gongs on the ship rose up. The send-offers and passengers were busy for a while. Only to see colorful paper circles, thrown at each other. In a moment, it was covered as dense as a spider web, fluttering in the wind, which was very interesting. At 10:00, the whistle blew, and the Dayang Maru moved slowly. The shouts of "pull" and the sound of铿锵 (keng qiang - sonorous) music gradually weakened. More than a thousand guests and athletes said goodbye for a while.

Buddhist Music Holding Buddha Chi Fo 198

Our country's local accents vary from place to place. The Wu dialect is soft, and the Central Plains dialect is grand. The Min and Yue dialects are different. Only when chanting Buddhist scriptures, singing praises to the Western Paradise, and hitting the fish-shaped woodblock and chime stones, the melodies are clear and loud, and the Brahman chants are sonorous, the whole country seems to be in the same rhythm. Some say that chanting Buddha is a matter of pure practice, so why bother with musical scales to promote the Buddha's name and sing Buddhist songs? In the Buddhist monastic rules, there is a saying that one should not engage in singing, dancing, or music. They do not know that music touches people most deeply. Chanting Buddha while striking the fish-shaped woodblock and chime stones, hitting the bell and beating the drum, is precisely to harmonize the mind and nature. The two characters "ritual" and "music" are the great methods for sages to govern the world, which the Confucians speak of in the most detail. In our Buddhist tradition, when selecting the perfect and complete root, the wise Manjushri chose the ear root alone. Guanyin attained enlightenment the earliest, and her cultivation was achieved from understanding the nature of hearing. The beings of the Saha world do not understand this principle. Some slander harmonious singing, and some denounce Buddhist music. Is this not a fallacy? One must know that chanting Buddha while harmonizing with musical scales was advocated by the fourth ancestor of the Lotus sect, Dharma Master Fazhao. The so-called Five Assemblies Great Assembly has a very profound meaning.

A'gang's Stomach Gu Lian 199

A'qiao saw an advertisement in the newspaper that Yantai Beer and Yili Soda were giving away free drinks at the New World, and sighed that it was a rare and cheap opportunity. He pulled A'gang to Bai Xiang (visit) at the New World. A'gang said to A'qiao on the road, "Spending two jiao xiaoyang, you can drink ten or eight bottles of beer and a dozen or half a dozen bottles of soda. The boss of that beer and soda company is too sacrificing. They must really be a'gang. I'm called A'gang, and I don't quite believe it." A'qiao said, "You're trying to be clever again. Such a big company wouldn't lie." When the two of them arrived at the New World, they saw many people crowded together, drinking as much as they wanted without limit. A'gang was so happy that he couldn't speak. He drank seven and a half bottles of beer in a row, and his stomach immediately bulged. He really couldn't hold any more, so he turned around to drink soda. A'qiao said, "You've already had your fill of beer. You can stop drinking soda for a while and come back to drink it later." A'gang thought for a moment and said, "Huh. My stomach for beer is full, but my stomach for soda is still empty." A'qiao laughed and said, "You're really a'gang. How can one person have two stomachs?"

Visiting a Scene from The Merchant of Venice

— Chang Yue

On the evening of a previous day, I visited director Ying Yunwei on a matter of business. It happened that the Drama Association was rehearsing the elopement scene from Shakespeare's great work, "The Merchant of Venice." I was very fortunate to have a preview. The play was translated from English and used pure Mandarin dialogue. In my humble opinion, translation is the most difficult part of literature. There is often a tendency to leave out the essence and keep the dross. Only this play can avoid its common defects. The wording and arrangement of the sentences are all suitable for our country's grammar. In addition, the actors' pronunciation is correct and the tone is clear, so everyone can understand it.

At the beginning of the scene, there were two people acting as lookouts to help with the elopement, holding torches and waiting for the protagonist, Lu Lun, so that they could go together. But Lu did not arrive for a long time. The two of them then made a lot of arguments, expounding the meaning of lovers' appointments and love. And the philosophy in it is also in line with the current situation of fashionable people in Shanghai. The indirect and subtle criticisms are incisive. If those who are fickle and opportunistic can hear this wonderful theory and not be ashamed to death, I don't believe it.

Then Lu hurried up, pointed to the mansion behind him in a low voice and said to his lookouts, "My father-in-law lives here." The appearance was quite appropriate. Suddenly, he saw a figure in the house, which seemed to be male, and was extremely frightened. Soon he realized that the man in the house was his lover, who had changed her hairpin for a cap. So the color of joy overflowed his eyebrows. The oaths of love and the subtlety of the two people's affection were exhausted. When they ran away, the atmosphere in the whole scene was very tense. It is appropriate to sneak away from people like this.

Overall, this scene was performed with emotion and reason, and was impeccable. All four actors were able to maintain their identity, and among them, the actor who played Lu Lun was the most rare. The actor has a delicate face and a strong body. He combines solemnity and humor. There are many similarities with the former movie star Valentino. In this scene, he showed the expressions of elation, fright, joy, and panic to perfection. The various transitions added a lot of color to the play. Director Ying has a discerning eye and found this talent. Is it really true that there is a Bole in the world before there is a thousand-mile horse? (Not paid)

Miscellany of Touring America by Zhui Yu Xuan Lai 200

We are about to set off for Chicago, where we are scheduled to perform for ten days. Then we will go to San Francisco and then to Honolulu. Then we will return to China. Wanhua has a strong ambition to tour Europe in one go, but the people traveling with her have been away from home for a long time and are eager to return, so she is hesitating. We will see what the situation is at that time and then decide. Although we have stopped performing and are resting these days, Wanhua is still busy. There are people painting portraits, taking photos, sculpting, news reporters, people in the theater world, and those who admire her and ask to see her. It is really like the road in Shanyin, and she is overwhelmed. And tea parties and banquets are still going on at the same time. In the evening, she went to various theaters to watch plays with Mr. Zhang Pengchun and others, enthusiastically studying.

On the evening of the 23rd, Wanhua hosted a banquet for people from all walks of life. Many people came. She said a few grand words at the banquet, saying that she was very grateful for the special welcome from all walks of life when she first came to your country. She hoped that the friendship between the two countries would be enhanced through artistic relations. She thanked the public for their praise of Chinese art on behalf of the Chinese art community. The guests left happily.

Wanhua has indeed lost a lot of weight, probably because she is too tired. But her spirit is still not reduced. Since she achieved great success here, she has been even more humble in her attitude. It is really admirable.

There is a great drama critic here named Mr. Yang Siarh Young. He is the most admiring of Wanhua's art. The day before yesterday, he gave her a ring that was a Roman artifact from five hundred years ago. There are very many other people who give her souvenirs.

Last year, I saw a Paris newsletter in a domestic newspaper. The International Drama Association was established in Paris. Dr. Xie Shoukang was the participant from our country. He proposed at the conference that Wanhua be invited to Paris next year (this year). At that time, the representatives of various countries were very supportive, but the cost was too great. Later, the president of the association, Mr. Momey (Director of the Second National Theater of France), discussed and planned to send a letter to major theaters along the way to Moscow and Berlin in the name of the association to invite her to perform, so that it would not be difficult. Now that there is a plan to tour Europe, it may be possible to contact them. But I am afraid that there is not enough time to prepare in a short time. We will have to talk about it after returning to China. A very large exposition will be held in Chicago next year. Someone wants to write a play with a world perspective for Wanhua and prepare to invite him to sing. They all say that it will be better than American actors. From this, we can also know the general admiration of the American mind.

Warmth in the Heart (1) (9) (3) — Bao Tianxiao 201

Chapter Eleven: Emerald Nets and Pearl Hairpins, a Fair Lady Returns to a Talented Man; Green Tent and Scarlet Curtains, a Famous Actress Marries into a Prominent Family

However, when a person's luck turns, naturally blessings arrive and their hearts are bright. Turning ugliness into beauty... Everyone who saw her superb acting skills and beauty said, "Her reputation is well-deserved." This time, the congratulatory performance for Liu Yinbo's wedding not only did not harm the old troupe of the theater that brought him to Shanghai, but also benefited them. Although they only watched one excerpt from "Fen He Wan", how could that be enough? When he officially took the stage three days later, the box seats and flower halls were sold out long in advance. They were booked for a week in advance. Because those who had seen the play at Wei Chun Yuan that day told those who had not seen his play, spreading the word to each other. The people of Shanghai are all fond of fresh novelties. Now that such a famous actress with both beauty and talent has come from Beijing, how could they not go and feast their eyes? Therefore, when Mei Lanfang came to Shanghai for the first time, from the day he took the stage, he sang for a full month. They also retained him for three more days to sing a farewell memento. There was not a single day that the theater was not sold out. That theater had already closed its iron gates at 9:00 PM. From then on, Mei Lanfang enjoyed great fame both in the north and south. It is said that after Liu Yinbo's wedding, they went to Hangzhou for their honeymoon according to Western customs. At that time, a certain major bank in Beijing was about to hire a banking expert. Knowing that Liu Yinbo had studied banking, they hired him. However, in the second half of the year, it was time for Liu Xingshu's wedding. Liu Xingshu's temperament and disposition were somewhat different from those of his elder brother. Yinbo was a magnanimous and open person, while Xingshu was a cautious and careful person. At that time, Yinbo had several positions in the north and wanted to persuade Xingshu to give up his work in the publishing house and newspaper office and come to the north to work. However, Xingshu was a little hesitant. It turned out that he was preparing for his own wedding. He was also preparing to get married in Shanghai. Since he was getting married in Shanghai, he naturally could not leave Shanghai for the time being. Moreover, he also had a temper. He wanted to do everything himself. It was not that he did not trust others, but he felt that he would feel more at ease if he did it himself. The first thing was the economic issue. He was a competitive person. He did not want to be too frugal in this wedding. His father was very fair to his two sons, subsidizing them each with one thousand yuan. In addition, since they were able to get married, they naturally had the ability to be self-reliant. Because their father, although he was engaged in business, was born poor and had no extra savings. If Xingshu wanted to ask his father to transfer some money from his business for his wedding, it would not be impossible. However, he was very unwilling to trouble his father with his wedding. According to him, since he was already a husband of more than twenty years old, he should be able to support himself. It would be best if he did not even need the thousand yuan from his father.

Commercial News 202

Finance: Interbank lending rates rise, liquidity in the dollar market eases

Market Overview: The volume of foreign currency transactions in recent days has been significantly higher than before, consistently exceeding 30,000 to 50,000 [units] daily. However, despite the active trading, the funds are ultimately being utilized within the local market and have not been exported. Consequently, neither prices nor market sentiment have shown a significant increase. Currently, the demand in other regions is primarily met by banknotes, with silver becoming a secondary commodity. As a result, interest rates on silver are unable to rise substantially. After a period of easy credit, the silver market has tightened again due to the higher volume of outward remittances.

Interest Rate Quotes: For "dollar interest," the early morning rate was two fen within the customs barrier, equivalent to 7 qian, 1 fen, 9 li, 8 hao, and 7 hu and a half. By the afternoon, it had risen to 7 qian and 2 fen. Although the fluctuation was only 1 hao and 2 hu and a half, it had lingered around the 2 fen mark for quite some time. "Silver interest" rose yesterday due to the substantial remittances required by banks, causing a slight tightening of the silver market. The early morning rate was 1 qian and 2 fen, and the afternoon rate was 1 qian and 3 fen, a significant improvement of 5 fen compared to the previous day. The "hua tou" (premium for silver) plus the water content naturally rose, becoming 1 qian and 3 or 4 fen. Bank rates also reached 5 fen in the market.

Subsidiary Coin Market Conditions: The market for "Jiangnan small dollars" remained mediocre. The early morning rate was 6 qian, 3 fen, and 6 [li], while the afternoon rate was 6 qian, 3 fen, and 8 [li]. The rates were the same for both sessions compared to the previous day's exchange. Consequently, the market price suddenly soared. The early morning rate was 6 qian, 0 fen, 2 li, 1 hao, and 2 hu and a half, while the afternoon rate reached 6 qian, 0 fen, and 4 li and a half, an improvement of 2 li, 3 hao, and 7 hu and a half compared to the previous day. The trading volume was 170,000 jiao in the early morning and 110,000 jiao in the afternoon. Copper coins also increased by 3,500 wen, reaching 406,000 wen.

Silver Inflow and Outflow: Yesterday, the banks' receipts and payments were uneven. Foreign banks had special receipts and payments of 2-3 million in notes and 2.3 million in cash. Foreign banks deposited 1.2 million into warehouses, while Chinese banks withdrew 500,000. Japanese banks received and paid out over 4 million in various funds and deposited 800,000 into warehouses. Money shops received and paid out 28 million in silver public bonds, 4 million in "hua tou" (premium for silver), and over 1.1 million in remittances from various routes, along with several hundred thousand in cash payments.

Golden Market Upheaval 203

Prohibition of Gold Bar Exports…Levying of Silver Tax

Bulls Suddenly Hit…Rushing to Exit

Nineteen Taels of Twists and Turns in the Gold Market

Total Drop of Eleven Taels and Eight [Qian] Yesterday

The Origin of the Reaction: Yesterday, there was a dramatic change in the gold market, with extremely chaotic and disorganized conditions. The price plummeted by over ten taels, with fluctuations of several taels at times. The morning session experienced nineteen taels of twists and turns, while the afternoon session still had seven taels of variations, making it difficult to predict. The reason for the sudden change was the government's sudden announcement of a ban on cash exports and the levying of silver tax. This caused a shock to the market, resulting in a strong reaction.

Forward Traders First Paid In, Then Paid Out: Yesterday was the forward rollover, marking the start of the July contract. The market opened at 8 o'clock, and trading began. Initially, those trading June for July paid in three or four qian, then settled, and finally, the bulls ended up paying out six or seven qian. By noon, it was only two qian. The situation was very confusing. There was no trading in the June contract, with most switching to the July contract. The opening price was 520 taels, and the closing price was 513 taels and 5 qian. Based on the July contract, this was a drop of 11 taels and 8 qian compared to the previous day, reversing the previous high prices. In the afternoon, price listings were generally posted.

Sudden Changes After the July Contract Entered the Market: The trading among dealers in the July contract was so chaotic that it was difficult to track. However, Wanxing, Shunli, Taixing, and others were buying, while Fuchang, Yuanmaoyong, Chengfengyong, and others were selling. Foreign exchange showed some decline, but not as significant as the change in gold prices. Bank purchases were still good. From the start of the morning session, the large bars shrank, immediately showing weakness, and then plummeted by over ten taels, suddenly reaching 501 taels. Rumors of a cash export ban spread, causing widespread panic. Later, buyers became active, and the price rebounded by over ten taels, but the market remained volatile. Afterwards, the market declined again, with turbulent waves. Firms such as Wanxing and Shunli continued to buy, while large firms such as Zhifengyong, Taixing, and Yuansheng aggressively sold. Eventually, the price fell below 510 taels. The price of British silver bars shrank by one-sixteenth to one-eighth, and the silver price decreased by three-eighths.

Lowest Drop to 01 Taels at 8:30: The July contract opened at 520 taels, with Fuchang and others rushing to sell, causing a rapid decline of 19 taels to around 501 taels at 8:30. Afterwards, buyers took advantage of the drop, causing a sudden jump of over 16 taels. Around 9:30, it was 17 taels and a half. The initial announcement was not updated, and it suddenly dropped to 13 taels and 5 qian. Then, it rose by 2 taels. Suddenly, there were more sellers, and the exchange rate seemed to weaken. By 10:00, it had fallen 4 taels to 510 taels. Afterwards, market sentiment eased. Zhengjin absorbed the July contract at 10 pence 625, Huashang Bank absorbed the June contract at 10 pence 5625, and Mitsui and Mitsubishi traded at 10 pence and a half. After 11:00, it rose to 15 taels and 4 qian, but the closing price at noon was 513 taels and 7 qian.

Afternoon Closing at 508 Taels: The afternoon session opened at 512 taels and a half, then rose from 12 taels to 14 taels and 2 qian due to the decline in the Indian exchange rate by 6-7 ounces. After 2:30, it declined slightly by 1 tael. At 3:00, news spread that a certain bank's shipment of cash had been rejected by customs, preventing export. Consequently, large firms such as Xinhang and Taixing aggressively sold, causing a sudden drop of 6-7 taels. After 3:15, it was 507 taels and a half, then rose by 3-4 taels. Due to the constant selling, the trend remained weak. At 4:00, it was 507 taels, 7 or 8 qian. Afterwards, there were occasional fluctuations of 1-2 taels, and the exchange market also weakened. The closing price at 4:30 was 508 taels. The maximum price fluctuation for the day was 20 taels, and the minimum was 1 tael, a difference of 19 taels. The posted price fluctuated by over 27-28 taels. The book prices for the June/July contracts were 514 taels in the morning session and 508 taels in the afternoon session. Due to the excessive fluctuations, there was a double settlement price. The water compensation was 516 taels in the morning and 510 taels in the afternoon. Early morning items opened at 21 taels, closed at 13 taels at noon, 11 taels in the afternoon, and closed at 08 taels and a half.

Dalian Firms Bought Approximately 10,000 Bars: In terms of trading by various firms, Taixing, Taifengcheng, Shunli, Wanxing, Cuitai, Xiangyu, and others were buying, while Yuanmaoyong, Chengfengyong, Yucheng Yong, Jiutai, Fuchang, and Yu Da were selling. Hengxing and Yuantai and Dadecheng had occasional inflows and outflows. In the afternoon, Xiangyu, Fuchang, Xieyu, Wanxing, and Shunli were buying, while Zhifengyong, Dadecheng, Yuansheng, and Yu Da were selling. Hengxing was buying. Chinese Merchants Dump English and American Contracts

Excessive Trading in Japanese Gold, Transactions Become Dull

No Changes in Listed Prices

Yesterday, the silver markets in England, America, India, and other countries all declined again. However, the markets in Yokohama and Kobe remained stagnant. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) listed prices remained unchanged. However, the English, American, and Japanese exchange rates showed significant changes within the banks, with chaotic and unpredictable fluctuations. This was due to the extraordinary changes in the gold market, which had been rising for five or six days before suddenly reversing. It had broken through 510 taels, with daily fluctuations of nearly 20 taels. However, the exchange rates did not show such drastic movements. Chinese speculators and gold dealers tended to sell to make contracts, with English gold trading volume reaching approximately 300,000-400,000 pounds. Banks still had strong demand. American gold also sold for approximately 1 million yuan. However, due to the significant difference between the bank's buying and selling prices for Japanese gold, no purchases were made, with only several hundred thousand yuan being sold. Banks such as Hefeng and Sumitomo absorbed slightly. Compared to the previous day, English exchange increased by 0.375, American exchange increased by 0.8125, and Japanese gold decreased by 0.01625. Market sentiment was extremely chaotic, and market conditions were unpredictable.

English Exchange: The internal market fluctuated throughout the day, with chaotic conditions. The May price was 1 shilling and 10 pence 5625, and the June, July, and August prices increased by 0625. The buying price also increased by 0625. The closing price at noon was 10 pence 4375 for May and 625 for August. The closing price in the afternoon was 10 pence and a half for May and 10 pence 6875 for August.

The closing price at noon was 45.5 yuan for May and 875 for August. The closing price in the afternoon was 45.75 yuan for May and 46.125 yuan for August.

Eastern Exchange: The internal market fluctuated irregularly. Trading was sluggish. The early morning price was 1 tael, 0 fen, 9 li, 375 for May, and the buying price was 25. June was 9 fen, and the buying price was 8 fen 875. July was 8 fen 625, and August was 8 fen 375, with a buying price of 25. The closing price at noon was similar. The closing price in the afternoon was 1 tael, 0 fen, 8 li, 5 for May, 8 fen 125 for June, 7 fen 75 for July, and 7 fen and a half for August. The buying price was reduced slightly by 125, it is said.

Recent Trend of Large Bars Falling Below Nineteen Pence 205

According to the London telegraph, the decline in the price of large silver bars continues to be severe. The forward price has fallen below the critical point of 19 pence, with the near-term price decreasing by 0.0625 to 19 pence (equivalent to 1 shilling and 10 pence 4375 for English gold) and the forward price decreasing by 0.375 to 18 pence 9375. Mainland China sold, and India bought. However, there was a shortage of near-term [silver], so the forward [silver] was sold. The market conditions were average. According to the New York telegraph, the price of American silver decreased by 0.375 to 4.075 yuan. English currency increased by 0.03125 against American currency to 4 yuan, 8 jiao, 5 fen, and 96875. American currency also increased by 0.03125 against English currency to 4 yuan, 8 jiao, and 6 fen. Japanese currency remained at 49.4375 yuan against American currency and 2 shillings 040625 against English currency. English-Shanghai exchange decreased by 0.125 to 1 shilling and 10 pence 375. The price of silver in Mumbai decreased by 4 ounces, with the spot price being 53 rupees, 14 ounces. The Reuters and Xinhua News Agency [reports] remained unchanged.

Yarn and Cotton: Weakness Increasingly Evident in Yarn Market 208

The yarn market remained weak and continued to show signs of decline. This was due to the unfavorable overall situation, weakness in overseas yarn markets, a sharp decline in the price of Three Grades Yarn, and softness in the American cotton market. Due to lack of sales, the local market was somewhat affected. However, buyers held on tightly and remained calm. Outsiders, seeing the stalemate, also refrained from taking action, leading to a lack of new transactions. Currently, the market is temporarily trending sideways. However, future developments are difficult to predict if the American cotton market changes or the war continues indefinitely.

Human Bidding Follows the Decline of Three Grades Yarn: The opening of the futures yarn market was uneventful. There were fewer buyers in the market. The second and third rounds of bidding were influenced by the decline in Three Grades Yarn, and sentiment eased. Prices for all months fell by 2-4 qian, except for the distant months. In the afternoon, the market remained weak, with retail investors selling. Dafeng, on the other hand, was selling heavily in the near months, causing a further drop of 3-6 qian. Total trading volume for the day was estimated at 6,200 bales. The closing prices for human bidding are listed below.

Silk and Tea: Silk Sales Stalled Due to Continued Shrinkage in Exchange Rates 211

Yesterday, the local foreign firm silk market continued to be stagnant. This was due to the further dramatic changes in the gold market, with prices soaring. The exchange rates of all countries, except for Japan, generally shrunk, resulting in a lack of silk telegraphs being sent to Shanghai. European firms remained hesitant. The new and old silk markets were completely stagnant. The shipment of new cocoons to Shanghai gradually improved. Given the current state of silk sales by foreign firms, the outlook for the silk market is increasingly pessimistic.

Declining Quality of Cocoons in Shaoxing 212

Shaoxing, Zhejiang Province, is a cocoon-producing region. Farmers regard sericulture as an important sideline and pay attention to rearing [silkworms]. In recent years, the abundance and quality of cocoons have surpassed other counties. There are as many as six or seven hundred cocoon shops in various regions. Every time cocoons are available, it is a grand occasion. This year, due to the unrest in various counties, the number of silkworms raised has been greatly reduced. Few cocoon shops have been rented out. After the silkworm farmers collected the eggs, the weather changed erratically, with sudden cold and heat, and continuous rain. By the time of the great sleep, the climate was still unfavorable, with thunderstorms and sweltering heat, and oddly cold yellow sand. This resulted in widespread silkworm diseases, with almost all local varieties being abandoned. Only the foreign varieties were relatively better. New cocoons are gradually entering the market. The statistical cocoon production in each county is less than 50%. The number of cocoon shops opening is less than 20-30% of previous years. The cocoon price is 40-45 yuan. High-quality goods are also only 50 yuan. Xiaoshan Dongxiang collects cocoons mostly with paper currency. Nanyang has not yet opened cocoon shops due to the famine, it is said.

Key News from Tea Markets in Tunxi, Wu, and Zhang 213

Tunxi New Tea Opens: The Tunxi tea market has recently become lively. All the shops along Yanghu Main Street have been rented out. Coarse tea opened on the 11th. High-grade [tea] is selling for 80 yuan, medium-grade [tea] for 68 yuan, and low-grade [tea] for 56-57 yuan. Tea prices are similar to last year. However, the harvest in various villages this year has been greatly reduced, and the price of rice is high. It is difficult to expect the market price to be low.

Standoff Between Firms, Few Openings: After days of negotiations, the new tea in Wu County is difficult to trade, as there is disagreement between the firms and they don't wish to compromise. Only the Shui Tea in the South Rural Area opened yesterday, with each load setting price at 65 yuan. Wucheng tea firms have been advancing the high-grade tea bought from Dexing, over a hundred loads, and price-point at 60 yuan. The rest are still in mutual consultation. Major merchants have been in a standoff for a few days. The firms in Shanghai have said that the news from the overseas tea market is bad, and have been advising not to procure excessive amounts, but the tea procurers have not been weakening. Thus, many merchants have sent tea specialists and clerks to take care of the business, and there are people going to Fuliang and East/South Rural Area to purchase, so the price of tea in Zhang Mountain will be difficult to suppress.

Zhang Mountain New Tea Begins Harvesting and Production: Zhang Mountain Green Tea, in the north of the county, is the highest grade in Wuyuan. The quality of the leaves and taste are unparalleled nationwide. Every time new spring tea is produced, merchants rush to order goods. Zhang Mountain tea is located on high mountain peaks, with a cold climate. The tea buds develop slowly. In recent months, it has been warm and rainy, and the growth has been faster than last year. The mountain residents are preparing to open their gardens and will begin harvesting and production within days. According to the mountain residents, due to its high location, Zhang Mountain tea is uniquely able to obtain morning dew and is delicate and fragrant. It is not like the loose tea produced in the plains.

Suian Green Tea Arrives in Shanghai 214

Yesterday, the foreign firm tea market in Shanghai was increasingly quiet. There were no transactions in Zhenmei Green Tea from native firms. Over 1,600 boxes of tea from Wenzhou had arrived, but the new price had not yet been announced. Over 100 boxes of Hongkou Black Tea were listed yesterday, but no deal had been reached. The new tea market is so quiet that it is heartbreaking. Yesterday, new samples of Zhenmei from Suian arrived at Chikaiyong and Rendeyong tea stores. More shipments will continue to arrive in Shanghai within days, it is said.

Grain: Rice Market Returns to Calm 215

Sales are Sluggish…Imported Rice Becomes Weak

Zhabei: Yesterday, the supply from the mainland remained scarce. However, the river inventory did not decrease. Market sales suddenly stalled. High-quality North Firm white japonica rice was also neither good or bad. Due to slow sales, stores were hesitant about average-quality Zhongguan rice. The price went from firm to stable. There were even fewer inquiries for old crops. Finally, it became weak and sluggish. There were few sales of Bo Dao rice, and the price remained unchanged. Suddenly, news spread that there would be a large supply of imported rice, causing stores in this area to stop sales, and the market stalled. Changes in the market were immobile, because they disliked how high priced the rice was. Diminished sales of inferior quality rice. The market situation for White Yuan rice was ordinary.

South Shanghai: There was not much supply from the river. The sales of Changxi North japonica rice were sluggish. However, high-quality goods were active, and the price still needed to be 20 yuan outside the customs. The Tong-grade machine rice market had fast sales in the morning and became stagnant in the afternoon. Due to the price increases in Zhabei the day before, the market was initially brisk but soon became sluggish. The price remained firm. The situation was the same for South Firm Bo Zao Dao and Yang Du Jian rice. Due to the stoppage of imported rice, it was difficult to sell the rice and change the circumstances. White Yuan rice sales were minimal, and the price was weak.

Recent Empty Squeeze in Flour Market 216

Jumps Up by One Fen and Seven and a Half…Distant Months Also Lifted

Yesterday, the flour market suddenly soared again. The empty squeeze situation seemed to be ripe for the picking. In the lean season, the market usually has no regular pattern. If you want to maintain stable prices, it depends on the adjustment of the manufacturers. One side tries to produce as much as possible to meet the demand, and the other side tries to reduce speculation to avoid hoarding goods. If the standard is squeezed up, the spot price will naturally rise. At a time when the cost of living is high, the burden on ordinary people will inevitably increase. Therefore, suppressing prices is the responsibility of the manufacturers. (It is said that the empty squeeze bulls have 500,000 bags in hand.) Distant months were also slightly lifted due to recent months, but the comparison was minimal. Regarding the exploitation of the May contracts, the five and a half qian per contract mark is still perceived to be at the lowest range. As a result, the May contracts increased by 1 fen 7 and a half compared to the day before, June increased by 7 and a half, August increased by 2 and a half, September increased by 5, and October remained unchanged.

Wheat Market Momentum Difficult to Sustain 217

Yesterday, the wheat market generally showed a fluctuating pattern. Although the quoted price of foreign wheat recovered by about two or three points, the recent exceptionally good weather has greatly benefited the prospects for the wheat harvest. Therefore, although domestic buyers are still resisting prices as usual, the overall environment makes it difficult to sustain further increases. As a result, the price for July was slightly better by one point, August was down by a slight point, and June and October remained unchanged. Currently, after the recent short squeeze on flour, traders seem to be contemplating speculative hoarding. This situation appears to be self-inflicted by the manufacturers. The asking price for delivered goods improved by two points compared to the previous day. Medium-grade goods remained stable. The opening price for wheat from Bengbu and Xuzhou was five taels, one mace, and two fen; wheat from Hankou was four taels, six mace, and five fen. A total of 2,300 bags were offered, which were reportedly purchased by Fuxin.

Piece Goods - Sales Slightly Brisk 218

The factory's sixteen-pound coarse cloth saw no movement from northern merchants, and inventories of brands such as Five Cranes, Five Old Men, and Double Elephant all fell by five points. Eleven-pound cloth was slightly firmer. Yesterday, merchants from Shantou and Xiamen bought over 150 pieces of brands like Three Deer, Three Cats, and Four Plain Lotus. Some transactions also occurred on this street. Three Deer and Three Cats were both priced at four taels, five mace, and seven and a half fen; Four Plain Lotus was priced at four taels, six mace, and two and a half fen. Among fine cloths, only Caiqiu was declining, but yesterday, spot goods had become scarce. Blue Flying Fish required seven taels and two mace due to increased purchases from Niuzhuang and Tianjin merchants. Trumpet Boy opened at six taels, eight mace, and seven and a half fen, a rise of two and a half fen compared to the previous day. The Ningbo merchants, after a period of stagnation, gradually became active yesterday.

Eastern and Western Piece Goods - Yesterday, sales showed a slight turnaround, mainly because the weather is getting hotter, and there is a sense that summer goods cannot be delayed any longer. Eastern goods like printed hemp gauze, raw foreign gauze, printed crepe, and white crepe saw brisk sales yesterday, with many transactions occurring on this street. White crepe opened at three taels, five mace, and five fen for Yin Pan, and two taels, nine mace, and seven and a half fen for Ren Gou. Banana Leaf Title Book Fine Stripe was at three taels and seven and a half fen. Prints were all sold at around two taels and four mace. Raw Straight Tribute Serge saw renewed interest from Hankou merchants, with Double Boy Deer at two mace, three fen, and five li, and Mount Mogan at two mace, six fen, seven li, and five hao. Fine cloth sales were quieter, with Signal Corps selling at eight taels, seven mace, and seven and a half fen; Moon Goose at eight taels, seven mace, and two and a half fen; and World Music Black at seven taels, seven mace and a half. Among Western goods, checkered hemp gauze was the most popular, priced at around two mace and four fen. Zhuluo gauze from Ruikang was at five mace and two and a half fen, and Taihe goods were at three mace and seven and a half fen, also with some transactions.

Saturday (3rd)

Shanghai Market 220

The Merchant of Venice Premieres Today

The Shanghai Dramatic Society's Shakespearean masterpiece, The Merchant of Venice, for which over three thousand yuan and two months of preparation were spent, will premiere today at the Central Auditorium on North Sichuan Road, near Yokohama Bridge. The matinee performance begins at 2:30 PM, and the evening performance opens at 7:30 PM. Only a few premium seats remain. Tickets will be sold at the door on a temporary basis, but seating is limited and will not be increased once sold out. To avoid crowding, audience members can pre-purchase tickets at the Modern Bookstore on Fourth Road, the New Book Monthly Store, and the Commercial Press bookstore in Hongkou. The play's sets and costumes are based on 16th-century Italy. The lighting equipment utilizes Gordon Craig's principles, with light levels that are harmonious and easy on the eyes. The courtship scene in the play has been translated into musical form, and renowned musicians and singers from Shanghai, including Tan Shuzhen, Shen Songbai, Zhu Xisheng, Pan Boying, Wang Yunjie, Liao Wenzhong, and Misses Luo Zhengya and Cheng Peizhi, have been specially invited to join the orchestra. The play's script is published by the New Book Monthly Store and will be sold in the theater. The Wrigley's Spearmint Gum Company is providing complimentary new candies with each ticket to enhance the audience's enjoyment.

Nineteenth Year of the Republic of China

The North Moon Music Bookstore, located at 463 North Sichuan Road, near Old Bazih Road, announces that it sells various musical instruments manufactured by the Shanghai North Moon Concert, whose exquisite craftsmanship has long been praised by the music community. To thank customers, a special discount of 10% off the original price will be offered for fourteen days.

The Yantai Beer and Yili Soda companies announce that, starting yesterday, they are jointly offering free drinks to customers at the northern section of the New World Entertainment Center, without restrictions. Approximately 20,000 entrance tickets were sold on the first day. The special issue magazine is creatively designed and includes masterpieces by famous artists such as Du He, Shou Juan, Zhuo Dai, and Ding Song, meticulously printed in Song-style font, making it very attractive. It is rumored to be included as a supplement to today's edition of "Saturday".

The Pathe Company announces that the famous actor Li Jirei, long hailed as a titan of the opera world, although he does not perform many plays, is exceptionally skilled in those he does. He has enjoyed a stellar reputation during his repeated visits to the South. On this occasion, the performance he has given in Shanghai is eagerly sought after by people from all walks of life. The Company, which has never shied away from business competition, has spared no expense to invite Mr. Li to record outstanding records, to share for the good of the public. Yesterday and the day before, he recorded many tracks including The Downfall of Luoma Lake, The Chain Plot, Asking Song Ling to Rescue Hongbi, and The Fengbo Pavilion. His voice is clear and resonant, with brilliant performances. The recording equipment used was newly purchased from overseas, so the clarity is exceptional, much like the beauty of the peony enhanced by its green leaves. Furthermore, Mr. Li himself stated that he is very satisfied with the recordings he made at Pathe, and that his performance of "The Downfall of Luoma Lake" even surpassed his usual live performances.
